Reference phase-11-learners-surface-decisions.md as canonical source.***

*v94 - Session 86 CLOSE — Notifications Phase 3 closeout SHIPPED end-to-end and verified; Phase 10 polish rounds 1, 2, 3, and 5 SHIPPED (Round 4 deferred to Session 87 for fresh recon). `results_available` firing-point wired via Postgres-only watcher trigger (no Edge Functions touched), `is_v1_active` flipped to true, all fixtures cleaned up; state restored to baseline. Phase 10 status: 4 of 8 surfaces shipped this session; 4 remain for Session 87+ (Round 4 Learning-admin tooling, Round 6 Notification surfaces, Round 7 Coach surfaces, Round 8 Mentor portal). (1) **`results_available` firing point SHIPPED — Postgres-only watcher trigger.** Constraint locked by Cole: do not touch any existing Edge Functions. Recovered the Session 84 paths-A-and-B notes via `conversation_search` (canonical docs had logged "documented" without the specifics). Cole rejected both Path A (fire from `calculate-scores` at row-insert with "results are ready to view" wording) and Path B (rearchitect NAI/AIRSA section generation to fire on true completion); proposed instead a row-count watcher on `facet_interpretations`. Discovery via diagnostic SQL: per-facet content is NOT stored as one row per facet — it lives inside `facet_interpretations.facet_data` JSONB arrays (one row per section bucket like `facet_insights_all`, with the array carrying the per-facet entries). `assessment_results.facet_insights_all_total` already tracks the expected per-context completion count (89 for `context_type='both'`, 47 for paired `professional`, 42 for paired `personal`). The completion contract: `jsonb_array_length(facet_data) >= facet_insights_all_total` on the `facet_insights_all` row. Verified live across all 7 PTP rows where the column is populated — every one matches exactly. (2) **Lovable review pass incorporated.** Cole sent the spec draft to Lovable for safety review. Lovable verified the dedup unique index is `(user_id, notification_type, dedup_key) WHERE dedup_key IS NOT NULL` — per-user not global — so taker and coach can safely share the same `dedup_key` string. Accepted refinements: instrument_label lookup via `instruments.instrument_name` (not hardcoded), JSONB type guard (`jsonb_typeof = 'array'`) before `jsonb_array_length`, per-call `BEGIN/EXCEPTION` blocks to isolate taker vs coach failures, `IF NOT FOUND THEN RETURN NEW` orphan guards on both `assessment_results` and `assessments` lookups, defensive `EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM users ...)` checks before each `notify_user` call. Rejected: `IS NOT DISTINCT FROM` short-circuit on UPDATEs (would short-circuit valid INSERTs because OLD is NULL; dedup_key already handles idempotency). Locked: Option A for paired PTPs — one notification per half (per `assessment_result_id`); UI-side collapse from Session 85 Option C2 handles the user-facing single-entity view. (3) **Two migrations applied + verified.** `session86_results_available_watcher_trigger` created the SECDEF function `fire_results_available_on_full_facets()` and the `trg_results_available_on_full_facets` AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE trigger on `facet_interpretations` gated to `WHEN section_type = 'facet_insights_all'`. `session86_results_available_activate_v1` flipped `notification_types_catalog.results_available.is_v1_active = true`. Zero existing user triggers on `facet_interpretations` (no collision risk). The dry-run sequence (deploy trigger → verify → flip flag) is safe because `notify_user` short-circuits at the `is_v1_active` check returning `'type_not_v1_active'` without inserting any row. (4) **Five fixture-based tests, all passed.** Cole declined to take a real PTP through the system; tests run by directly inserting fixture rows that match the trigger's expected shape. Test 1 (dry-run, flag off): trigger fired, `notify_user` returned `type_not_v1_active`, zero notifications landed. Test 2 (flag on, taker only, `context_type='both'`, total=89, array_len=89): notification landed for taker with correct payload — `instrument_label="Personal Threat Profile"` resolved via `instruments` table lookup, not hardcoded fallback. Test 3 (flag on, coach-ordered via `ordered_by_coach_id=2f591eb3-...` Test Coach 2): both taker AND coach got notifications sharing the same dedup_key `results_available:<ar_id>` — validates the per-user unique index. Test 4 (idempotency): re-firing trigger via UPDATE on existing facet row produced zero duplicate notifications — both users remained at exactly 1 row for the shared dedup_key; `notify_user`'s `unique_violation` handler is doing its job. Test 5 (non-PTP gate): inserted NAI (INST-002) fixture with `facet_insights_all_total=25` and `array_len=25`; trigger fired, `instrument_id <> 'INST-001'` gate held, zero notifications landed. (5) **All fixtures cleaned up.** Four assessment_results, four assessments, four facet_interpretations rows, and three landed user_notifications all deleted in reverse-FK order. Baseline notification count restored exactly (`testclientbwe+employee@gmail.com` went from 10 → 10). Database state matches pre-Session-86 except for the new function, trigger, and flipped catalog flag. (6) **v1 coverage scope: PTP only.** NAI / AIRSA / HSS do not populate `facet_insights_all_total` (all NULL for those instruments); the trigger silently passes them. Wiring those instruments requires either their respective generation EFs populating `facet_insights_all_total` (or equivalent threshold column) OR a per-instrument completion contract. Both deferred — the AIRSA facet-generation gap investigation (Session 84 deferred item) is a prerequisite for AIRSA coverage. (7) **Standing rule candidate (§119): completion-watcher trigger pattern.** When a notification needs to fire at "true completion" of a server-side process that writes a deterministic completion threshold (count, status, etc.), prefer a Postgres trigger reading that threshold over editing the producing EF — provided the threshold column is already maintained by the EF and the completion contract is enumerable. Pattern: AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE trigger with WHEN-clause filter, SECDEF function checking threshold against array_length/row_count, dedup_key on `notify_user` for fire-once-per-target. No EF edits; deploy is reversible via DROP TRIGGER + flag flip. (8) **Notifications Phase 3 is now CLOSED.** All 18 catalog types have been reviewed; 17 are wired (16 active + `results_available` activated this session); 1 (`cert_path_deadline_approaching`) remains explicitly deferred as a v2 informational feature with no documented firing path. Two surfaces displaying "In Progress" can warrant different colors if one means "you are doing it" and the other means "someone else is doing it and you are waiting." *v93 - Session 85 CLOSE — five production bug clusters SHIPPED end-to-end and verified; cohorts formally deferred indefinitely; module reorder gap discovered + scoped + deferred to a fresh session. Backend-first throughout. Six backend migrations applied + verified (one full-rewrite RPC attempt was rolled back and replaced with a surgical edit before any production traffic hit it), one new SECURITY DEFINER RPC created, multiple Lovable PRs (Cole runs all Lovable; GitHub MCP is READ-ONLY). Carried Session 84 priorities (notifications Phase 3, Phase 10 polish, Group C closeable) NOT advanced — Session 85 was a production bug cluster session; they carry forward to Session 86 unchanged. Cohorts formally confirmed not needed and marked deferred (Q11 scoped them as schema-seam only; v1 UI was always a non-goal; Group C is closeable without them). (1) **Bug 1 SHIPPED — coach actor-order gate fix (Caroline / Patrice / Ryan).** Three production coaches with `coach_certifications.status = 'in_progress'` (not yet `certified` but holding non-zero `free_assessment_uses` cert-pool credit) were blocked at three frontend gates in `src/pages/coach/CoachClients.tsx`. Existing gates only checked `certified`. Pure frontend fix via Lovable: introduced derived booleans `canOrderAssessment` (certified OR in_progress-with-pool) and `actorOnlyMode` (forces modal into actor-debrief flow when coach is not certified but has pool credit). Modal force-sets `isActorDebrief = true` on submit. Plus a toast typo fix ("3 actor debriefs" → "4"). No backend touched. Standing rule candidate (§114): UI cert-status gates must distinguish "no cert" from "in-progress with active cert-pool credit"; `canDoFeature = certified || (in_progress && hasActivePool)`. (2) **Bug 2 SHIPPED — module archive CHECK constraint extension.** Module-tier archive cascade was failing because `content_assets.archive_reason` CHECK did not whitelist `module_archived`, `curriculum_archived`, or `certification_path_archived`. Cascade attempted to write the reason, hit the CHECK, transaction rolled back. Migration `session85_content_assets_archive_reason_check_extend_tier_cascade_reasons` dropped the old constraint and recreated with the 8-value whitelist (3 new tier-cascade values added — `module_archived`, `curriculum_archived`, `certification_path_archived` — alongside the 5 pre-existing values `content_item_archived`, `lesson_block_replaced`, `replaced_by_author`, `manual_archive`, `orphaned_pending_expired`). Standing rule candidate (§115): tier-archive cascades must whitelist the tier's `archive_reason` in the CHECK before the cascade trigger reaches the row. (3) **Bug 3 SHIPPED — My Learning blank cert-path tile (Symptom 1 RPC + Symptom 2 RLS gap).** User reported a cert-path tile on My Learning rendering with no name, no description, orange-circle placeholder thumbnail. Two independent defects under one symptom. **Symptom 1 — `get_user_learning_state` RPC was not projecting cert-path tier's `name`/`description`/`thumbnail_asset_id` as flat columns.** First attempt fully rewrote the function and accidentally introduced a `GROUP BY` bug. Caught during verification (no production traffic hit it). Recovered via `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` lookup of the Group Z m4 known-good source (version `20260516010830`), then applied a surgical edit. Three migrations: `session85_get_user_learning_state_project_flat_tile_fields` (BROKEN attempt), `session85_revert_get_user_learning_state_to_z_m4` (rollback to last-known-good), `session85_get_user_learning_state_add_flat_tile_fields` (surgical fix — LEFT JOIN to `certification_paths` in v_assignments CTE, flat name/description/thumbnail in v_assignment_rows via `COALESCE(cp_*, curriculum_*)`, same flat fields in v_module_assignment_rows). Lesson locked: surgical edits to complex RPCs with diff against live function definition; no full rewrites from memory (process discipline, not a §-numbered rule). **Symptom 2 — trainee tier-thumbnail RLS gap.** After Symptom 1 shipped, tile still rendered the placeholder. Root cause: `content_assets_trainee_read` RLS policy anchored its EXISTS chain on `content_items`. Tier thumbnails (cert_path, curriculum, module, resource) have `content_item_id IS NULL`. EXISTS returned false; trainees could not read thumbnail asset metadata even though bytes are public-tier per §84. Two migrations: `session85_align_content_asset_refs_trainee_read_status_filter` (`status = 'active'` → `IN ('active', 'completed')`) and `session85_create_get_thumbnail_urls_for_entities_rpc` (new SECDEF RPC `get_thumbnail_urls_for_entities(p_entity_type text, p_entity_ids uuid[])` returning `[{entity_id, asset_id, bucket, path, dominant_color}]`; branches per entity_type — cert_path/curriculum/module require `is_published = true AND archived_at IS NULL` and accept any authenticated user; resource branch mirrors `get_user_resources` is_visible rules with super_admin bypass). Frontend shipped via Lovable: new `resolveTierThumbnailUrls`/`resolveTierThumbnailRows` helpers in `src/lib/assetUrls.ts`, called from 5 sites — `MyLearningTab.tsx`, `ResourceGridTab.tsx`, `CertPathDetail.tsx`, `CurriculumDetail.tsx`, `ModuleDetail.tsx`. Standing rule candidate (§116): thumbnails are public-tier per §84; RLS on metadata when bytes are world-readable is the wrong protection model; SECDEF RPC enforcing "entity published AND not archived" at the API layer is the correct architecture. (4) **Bug 4 SHIPPED — coach can't see client results (Fix A + Fix B-Level-2 + Fix B-Level-3).** Cheryl Kish (`cf3ccc21-...`) could not load Edgar Vazquez Encarnacion's (`db586ec5-...`) PTP results — page flashed empty. Root cause: `src/pages/MyResults.tsx` line 437 queried `coach_clients_client_view`, which filters `WHERE client_user_id = auth.uid()` — correct for client callers, wrong for coach callers. Three related fixes shipped in one Lovable PR: **Fix A** — `MyResults.tsx` line 437: `.from("coach_clients_client_view")` → `.from("coach_clients")`; base table's RLS handles coach access correctly. **Fix B-Level-2** — `src/pages/coach/ClientResults.tsx` Level 2 `AssessmentList` data fetch: extended linked-id union to include `paired_assessment_id` so paired PTP sibling rows surface in the tile list. **Fix B-Level-3** — `CoachResultsView` permission resolver: `.eq("assessment_id", X)` → `.or(\`assessment_id.eq.${X},paired_assessment_id.eq.${X}\`)`; clicking a paired/personal tile no longer degrades to `score_summary`. Cheryl→Edgar verified end-to-end via impersonation. Edgar's `coach_clients` row: id `5ade7a72-3ce3-4bd5-a819-a04fdb07cf72`, `assessment_id = f0be3170-59d0-4aa2-8bd8-f9911bb35a16` (professional), `paired_assessment_id = 02079f1b-b119-4e73-a581-a678d1cdda38` (personal), `context_progress = 'both_done'`. Standing rule candidate (§117): `coach_clients_client_view` is for client callers exclusively; coach callers query the base table. (5) **Bug 5 SHIPPED — PTP paired-assessment UX consistency (Option C2).** Polish issue surfaced after Bug 4: Cheryl saw two visually identical "Personal Threat Profile / 5/14/2026" tiles; Edgar's own dropdown showed two entries "PTP Professional" / "PTP Personal". Same underlying data, inconsistent UX shapes across coach and client surfaces. Decision locked — **Option C2**: paired PTP collapses to ONE user-visible entity on BOTH surfaces. Coach tile labeled "Personal Threat Profile / Professional + Personal · {date}". Client dropdown shows ONE umbrella entry; if only paired PTP and no other instruments, dropdown hides entirely (the in-PTP tabs ARE the navigation). Lovable diagnose-then-implement cycle, two file changes. **`ClientResults.tsx` Level 2** — extended `AssessmentInfo` with `context_type`, `paired_assessment_id`, `instrument_id`; added `assessments` lookup for context info; grouping pass with mutually-paired check (prevents retake collapse); tile subtitle renders "Professional + Personal · {date}" for paired and "{Context} · {date}" for single; click handler always sends professional `assessment_id`. **`MyResults.tsx` dropdown** — extended fetch with `paired_assessment_id`; built `dropdownEntries` memo collapsing pairs; visibility gate switched from `assessments.length > 1` to `dropdownEntries.length > 1`; selected paired entry uses professional `result.id`. Did NOT touch `effectiveSelected`, PTP tabs, Combined synthesis, narrative providers, PDF export, narrative status polling, `ptpContextTab` initialization, AI chat session anchoring, or the "Complete other half" prompt. Mutually-paired check (each side's `paired_assessment_id` mirrors the other) protects against retake collapse — two professional retakes can never collapse. Standing rule candidate (§118): paired-PTP collapse uses mutually-paired check, not instrument equality. (8) **RPC wrapper shape discipline (§111 reinforce).** Session 85 verified the discipline held across all backend work — every RPC returning a wrapper object had a proper TypeScript interface at the call site, never cast wrapper-to-array via `as unknown as`. Standing rule from Session 84 (§111) reinforced as operational. (9) **Surgical edit process discipline locked (candidate standing rule, not §-numbered).** When a non-trivial RPC needs a small change, the correct approach is a diff against the live function definition (read via `pg_get_functiondef` or migration history) and a surgical edit. Full rewrites from memory introduce regression risk. Session 85 hit this on `get_user_learning_state` and recovered cleanly via the migration history lookup. Discipline: show diff against current restored function before applying; never rewrite from memory. (10) **Pattern: production bug clusters batch effectively into one session.** Five bug clusters (Bugs 1-5) shipped sequentially in Session 85, each with its own diagnose-then-implement cycle through Lovable. The session was high-bandwidth because each bug had clear ownership (frontend-only vs migration-only vs both), independent verification paths, and no shared regression risk. (8) **CSS bug surfaced post-merge — bare hex colors are NOT valid in `background-image`.** User reported every hero rendered navy regardless of the extracted dominant color. Diagnosis: bare hex colors like `#481a69` are NOT valid values for CSS `background-image` — only `<url>` and `<gradient>` are accepted. The invalid declaration was being ignored entirely, leaving the transparent overlay gradient to show the underlying page navy background through it. **Fix shipped via Lovable hotfix PR:** split the composed value across two CSS properties — `backgroundImage` (gradient layers only) and `backgroundColor` (solid hex or `transparent`). `const heroBackgroundImage = heroMeta?.dominantColor ? heroOverlay : \`${heroOverlay}, ${heroFallback}\`; const heroBackgroundColor = heroMeta?.dominantColor ?? "transparent";` Style prop now passes both. User confirmed fix shipped and working — heroes render in their dominant color across all detail pages. Build queue item: **Trusted Device feature for super-admin MFA step-up.** Build `trusted_devices` table (hashed token, fingerprint, label, expiry, revoked_at), `mint_trusted_device`/`check_trusted_device`/`revoke_trusted_device` RPCs, edit `impersonation-start` to read device cookie and bypass `check_mfa_freshness` on hit, "Manage trusted devices" settings page, auto-revoke on password/MFA changes, audit rows in `super_admin_audit_log`. Audit log analysis (`super_admin_audit_log` action_type=`certification_path_updated`) reconstructed: May 19 17:02:17 — upload `7a4f6a68-...` succeeded; May 19 17:02:56 (+39s) — `publishing` action wrote `thumbnail_asset_id=null` (`before_value` had asset, `after_value` was null); the `_archive_thumbnail_ref_and_maybe_asset` cascade correctly archived the orphan asset. **Conclusion: cascade-archive system working correctly.** Bug is editor-side: `CertPathEditor` (and CurriculumEditor / ModuleEditor / ContentItemEditor / ResourceEditor — all share the FileUploadField + state + upsert pattern) loses local thumbnail state between upload and save/publish. Build queue item: **Editor thumbnail-loss-on-republish hardening.** Options: (a) On save, if `thumbnailAssetId` is null AND `initial?.thumbnail_asset_id` was not null, show confirmation dialog. (b) Refetch the row fresh before submitting, merge any field where the form would null out a previously-populated value. Investigate whether the editor's `initial` data refetches after upload-finalize Edge Function returns. (11) **Pattern reinforced — fast diagnostic path for "feature broken" reports.** When a feature renders wrong despite the data being correct in the DB, the standing diagnostic sequence is: (a) verify the data IS correct in the DB (`execute_sql`); (b) simulate the exact query the frontend runs against the deployed REST endpoint with a real auth token and inspect the response shape; (c) if response shape is correct, inspect the rendering layer for the bug. The Session 84 CSS bug was found at step (c) — backend was correct (verified Cheryl's cert path = `#152c48` in the DB, the frontend query returned the right shape, the `heroBackground` string was built correctly) but the resulting CSS string was invalid by spec. *v91 - Session 83 CLOSE — super-admin manual completion control SHIPPED end-to-end; reverse-recount bug found during testing and FIXED; one Edge Function deployed to v2; full security-scan triage pass completed. Backend-first throughout. (1) **Super-admin manual completion control SHIPPED (Priority 1, carried from Session 82).** A super admin can mark any learning entity complete OR incomplete across four tiers — content item, module, curriculum, cert path — from the UI. An existing forward-only rollup trigger chain cascades completions upward; this feature adds the deliberate-override path. **Four design decisions locked before code:** (a) reverse cascade stops at the curriculum tier — a reverse that would drop a curriculum under an already-certified cert path is REFUSED entirely (`manual_incomplete_blocked_certified_cert_path`); (b) combined-cert cascade is out of scope by construction since reverse never reaches `coach_certifications`; (c) forward marks the full subtree complete, reverse is target-plus-ancestor recompute and never touches children; (d) forward CAN certify via rollup, reverse can NEVER un-certify — the cert tier reuses the existing `grant_certification`/`revoke_certification` RPCs. (2) **Migration 1 `manual_completion_control_action_types`** — three audit `action_type` rows in `super_admin_action_types`, per §99, INSERTed before the RPCs that emit them. (3) **Migration 2 `manual_completion_control_rpcs`** — three public RPCs (`set_content_item_completion(p_user_id, p_content_item_id, p_complete, p_reason)`, `set_module_completion(p_user_id, p_module_id, p_complete, p_reason)`, `set_curriculum_completion(p_assignment_id, p_complete, p_reason)`) plus three internal helpers. All SECURITY DEFINER, search_path locked, `assert_super_admin` + `assert_impersonation_allows('permission_change')` + reason >=10 chars, idempotent, audit-logged. The curriculum RPC is keyed per-assignment (`p_assignment_id`), not per-curriculum, because a curriculum can be assigned more than once. (4) **Migration 3 `manual_completion_helpers_revoke_authenticated`** — the three internal helpers made service_role-only (REVOKE from authenticated), defense-in-depth so only the public RPCs are the reachable surface. (5) **Migration 4 `manual_completion_reverse_recount_fix` — the reverse-recount bug fix (see item 7).** (6) **Migration 5 `storage_policies_content_and_skills_buckets` — the security-pass storage migration (see item 9).** (7) **BUG FOUND during testing + FIXED + verified — reverse-recount.** Testing the new feature on Test Coach 4 surfaced a real bug: the `set_module_completion` and `set_curriculum_completion` reverse paths hard-wrote a downgraded status (`not_started`/`active`) instead of recomputing the tier from its children, producing incoherent states (a `not_started` module sitting above six completed required items). **Decision locked — Option A:** module and curriculum status must ALWAYS be recomputed honestly from children, never hard-written; you change a parent\'s status by changing its children, not by overriding it. Migration `manual_completion_reverse_recount_fix` rewrote both reverse branches to recount inline; "mark incomplete" on a tier whose children are all complete is now a no-op returning `changed:false` plus a `note`. Test Coach 4\'s two corrupted rows were repaired to `completed`. The bug got through the original Migration 2 verification because the test matrix tested reverse-from-below but never reverse-at-the-tier — a test-matrix hole, now closed. (8) **Frontend SHIPPED via Lovable — the Completion Control tab + a follow-up.** A fourth "Completion Control" tab on `LearningAdmin.tsx`; a SEPARATE admin learning-tree component (NOT an edit of the shared `MentorProgressTree.tsx` — ~150 lines of duplication accepted to keep the mentor-portal blast radius at zero); an artifact inspector showing each of the eight content-item types\' real submission per a data-source table; a confirm dialog; impersonation-aware disabling of mark actions. New files under `src/components/learning-admin/`. The three `set_*` RPCs are called with an `as never` cast (not yet in generated `types.ts`). **Follow-up prompt:** `CompletionConfirmDialog` was discarding the RPC result and always showing "Marked complete/incomplete" — it now captures `data` and branches the success toast on `data?.changed === false` to a neutral "No change" toast carrying the backend `note`; the cert-path branch uses a strict `=== false` check and is unchanged. (9) **Edge Function `content-item-file-upload` v1->v2 deployed (verify_jwt:false preserved).** The `read` action now accepts an OPTIONAL `target_user_id`; when present and not equal to the caller it is passed to `get_content_item_for_viewer`, which gates on super_admin/mentor; absent, the function is byte-identical to v1. Reason: a super admin needed to view another learner\'s uploaded file in the new artifact inspector — v1 was hardwired to the caller\'s id. Verified by logic + probe (anon -> 401, super-admin resolves another user\'s item, non-privileged caller rejected). NOT yet verified by a live signed-URL browser round-trip — carried. CARRYOVER: v2 source owed to GitHub `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` at `supabase/functions/content-item-file-upload/index.ts`. (10) **Security-scan triage pass — three errors + six warnings dispositioned.** The Lovable scanner (flagged "Out of date") fired; Lovable did an independent diagnose-only pass; Claude verified every claim against the live DB; the two sides agreed a fix split — Claude does backend, Lovable does frontend. **E1/E3 (storage buckets with no policies) — REAL defense-in-depth gap, FIXED this pass.** `content-item-file-uploads` and `skills-practice-attachments` had zero `storage.objects` RLS policies. Not exploitable (RLS-on + no policy = default deny held; the Edge Functions use service-role and bypass storage RLS anyway), but a missing floor inconsistent with every other content bucket. Migration `storage_policies_content_and_skills_buckets` added eight path-segment ownership policies (four per bucket). Path layouts verified against live objects: content bucket `{contentItemId}/{userId}/{file}` -> user is segment 2; skills bucket `{contentItemId}/{role}/{userId}/{file}` -> user is segment 3, role is segment 2. Skills SELECT keys on segment 3 (a trainee may see both their own `trainee/` file and the `mentor/` feedback file under their own id — already an entitlement); skills write policies additionally require segment 2 = `trainee` so a trainee cannot write the mentor path. Behaviorally verified. Path-segment match was chosen over the scanner-suggested table join — simpler, no per-access subquery, consistent with the existing `departure-exports` policies. **E2 (quiz answers readable) — NOT a bug.** `quiz_answer_options` has only service_role + super_admin policies, no authenticated/public SELECT; `is_correct` is locked; the trainee path is `get_quiz_for_trainee`, which strips it. The scanner asked us to confirm a negative; confirmed. Mark fixed in scanner. **W1/W2/W3 (three XSS) — REAL, moderate severity (writers are super-admin-only), FIXED by Lovable.** `isSafeHttpUrl` in `src/lib/safeUrl.ts` is now the single allowlist used by all three href sites (`ExternalLinkViewer.tsx`, `ResourceReader.tsx` VideoEmbed, `BlockRenderer.tsx` button-block — the third found by Lovable\'s own audit) and both TipTap `Link.configure` sites; resource articles sanitized via DOMPurify with `USE_PROFILES:{html:true}`. **W4/W5/W6 (cohort/bulk-batch SELECT) — design-intentional/deferred per the Session 73 dispositions; no work.** PENDING for Cole: mark E2/W4/W5/W6 ignored in the scanner with rationale, then re-run the scan to confirm it clears. *v90 - Session 82 CLOSE — Mentor-role feature SHIPPED end-to-end; actor-flow + coach-invitation email bugs FIXED. Backend-first throughout. Two backend migrations for mentor-role, two backend migrations for actor flows, one Edge Function path change verified, two Lovable prompts written for Cole to run (one mentor-role frontend, one combined actor-debrief + self-pay email frontend). Priority 2 (super-admin manual completion control) was NOT reached — the session budget went to Priority 1 plus actor-flow firefighting; it carries to Session 83 as priority 1. Priority 4 (notifications) did not start. (1) **Mentor-role model decision LOCKED — Model 1, standalone eligibility flag.** There was no standalone "mentor role" before this session — being a mentor was emergent from a `coach_mentor_assignments` row. Two models were presented: Model 1, a standalone `users.is_mentor` eligibility flag (schema change); Model 2, a cleaner UI over the existing `coach_mentor_assignments` flow (no schema change). Cole chose Model 1. Rationale: without an eligibility flag there is no clean way to gate the `/mentor` route or to enforce that only approved users can be assigned as mentors. This refines — does not contradict — the v84 "mentor is a relationship row" framing: the relationship rows still define WHICH trainees a mentor mentors; the new flag defines WHETHER a user is allowed to be a mentor at all. (2) **`list_mentor_trainees` confirmed leak-safe.** Read via `pg_get_functiondef` (it was NOT read in Session 81 — flagged carryover). Confirmed: a non-mentor caller gets `viewer_role:"none"` and an empty roster; no other trainee's data is exposed. No fix needed. (3) **Migration 1 — `users.is_mentor` column + helper, applied + verified.** New `is_mentor` boolean column, NOT NULL, default false. Backfilled `true` for the one existing approved mentor (Test Coach 1) and false for everyone else. A small read-helper added with clean grants (no anon/PUBLIC). Verified column, index, backfill scope, helper grants, and gate via separate `execute_sql`; no function overload created. (4) **Migration 2 — `set_mentor_role` RPC + `mentor_role_changed` audit action_type, applied + verified.** Per §99 the new action_type is INSERTed in the SAME migration as the RPC that emits it, or `log_super_admin_action` FK-fails. `set_mentor_role(p_user_id uuid, p_is_mentor boolean, p_reason text)` — one RPC handles BOTH grant and revoke via the boolean param; SECURITY DEFINER, `assert_super_admin` + `assert_impersonation_allows('permission_change')` + reason ≥10 chars; logs a single `mentor_role_changed` action with before/after JSON showing the transition; idempotent — a redundant call returns `changed:false` with no error. Returns jsonb `{user_id, is_mentor, changed}`. The `mentor_role_changed` action_type: category `admin_role_management`, tier2, requires MFA + justification, mutation, denylisted during impersonation — mirrors the `mentor_assigned` precedent. RPC grants restricted to `authenticated`/`service_role`, single signature. Positive end-to-end test: grant flipped the flag, the audit row landed (proving the §99 FK chain), the redundant-grant no-op returned `changed:false`, revoke restored a clean state — no residual test rows. (5) **`assign_mentor` now gates on `is_mentor`.** The existing `assign_mentor` RPC was updated so assigning a user as a mentor of a trainee requires that user to have `is_mentor = true`; an un-approved user surfaces the friendly `mentor_not_approved` error. (6) **Mentor-role Lovable prompt written (frontend-only, Cole runs it).** Six changes: surface `is_mentor` through `useUserProfile`; derive an `isMentor` boolean in `accountRoles.ts` (mirrors `isPractitionerCoach`); NEW `MentorGuard.tsx` (allows `isMentor || isSuperAdmin`); swap the two `/mentor` routes from `PractitionerCoachGuard` to `MentorGuard` in `App.tsx`; gate the "Mentor Portal" sidebar entry on real mentor status in `AppSidebar.tsx`; add an "Assign Mentor Role" tab to `LearningAdmin.tsx` (searchable user list, grant/revoke via `set_mentor_role` through a reason dialog). This FIXES the Session-81 logged BUG-HIGH "any coach can reach `/mentor`". (7) **BUG FIXED + verified — actor-debrief paywall.** A certification trainee who invites an "actor" (practice subject) to take the PTP — the actor reached the assessment page and was shown a payment dialog ("Your Coach Wants You to Take This"). An actor debrief is free, covered by the trainee's certification. Root cause: in `InstrumentSelection.tsx` the `selfPayCoachClientsRes` query selects `coach_clients` rows with `stripe_payment_intent_id IS NULL` and treats every such row as "client must self-pay" — but an actor-debrief invitation legitimately has a null payment intent (it never involves Stripe), so it was swept into `selfPayCoachInstrumentIds` and triggered the paywall. **`start_assessment` was read in full and has NO payment gate of its own** — the paywall is purely a frontend display decision; there is no backend security hole. Backend fix (applied + verified): `coach_clients_client_view` now exposes the `invitation_source` column via `security_invoker`; testactor3 reading their own row sees `invitation_source = 'actor_debrief'`, `stripe_payment_intent_id = NULL`. Frontend fix is a Lovable prompt routing `invitation_source = 'actor_debrief'` rows (UUID-keyed, matching the existing `selfPayCoachInstrumentIds` keying) to a free-access branch. (8) **BUG FIXED + verified — actor-debrief invitation email never sent.** `handleOrderActorDebrief` called the internal-secret-protected `send-email` Edge Function directly from the browser, which cannot supply `INTERNAL_FUNCTION_SECRET`. Fix (Option B, chosen over reproducing the email template as a PL/pgSQL literal): `create_actor_debrief_order` migrated to a 5-arg signature adding `p_email_html` (DEFAULT NULL, backward-safe) and now sends the email server-side via `net.http_post` to `send-email` with the Vault secret + `x-internal-secret` header, copying the `notify_user` pattern. The Vault secret was verified readable + non-empty first. The email send is wrapped in a `BEGIN...EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS` block so an email failure NEVER rolls back a valid order; outcome reported in the return JSON as `email_dispatched`. The old 4-arg overload was DROPPED so all calls (including the frontend's current 4-arg call) resolve to the 5-arg version. Functional test confirmed `email_dispatched:true` — the `net.http_post` fired with the internal secret. (9) **BUG FIXED + verified — self-paid coach invitation email never sent.** Same browser-cannot-call-`send-email` cause as (8), in `handleOrderClientPays`. Confirmed broken by Cole's test plus the absence of any `handleOrderClientPays` success row in `email_logs`. Fix: a NEW generic RPC `send_coach_invitation_email(p_to, p_subject, p_html, p_email_type)` does the server-side `net.http_post` with the Vault secret, role-gated to coach / practitioner-coach / super-admin (not a wide-open mailer); returns `{dispatched}`; does not raise on email failure. A combined Lovable prompt updates `handleOrderActorDebrief` (pass `p_email_html`, drop the `send-email` invoke) and `handleOrderClientPays` (call `send_coach_invitation_email` instead of `send-email`). (10) **Coach-paid invitation email — UNVERIFIED, carried.** Sent server-side from the `stripe-webhook` Edge Function, which is not in the repo and could not be read this session; testing it would require a live charge. It runs server-side so it likely does not have the (8)/(9) bug, but this is not confirmed. Carryover: read the `stripe-webhook` source next session and verify its email logic. (11) **`create-checkout` graceful-degradation hardening — known unfixed, recurs ~60 days.** `create-checkout` throws a 500 instead of degrading gracefully when a comp coupon goes bad (expires/archives/deletes). Works today — Cole recreated the comp coupon unlimited and tested coach-paid checkout end-to-end — but comp coupons expire by design (`redeem_by` 60 days out), so this exact failure recurs. Logged HIGH with a known recurrence date; carried to Session 83. (12) **`3 of 3 → 4 of 4` cap display fix** — Cole ran this Lovable prompt; counted done. *v89 - Session 81 CLOSE — Group V certification buildout reached partially; password reset production bug fixed; coach-enrollment RPC fixed (Issue 2); marquee verified end-to-end; certificate + marquee-overflow fixes prompt-ready. (1) **Password reset production bug FIXED + verified live.** Real users clicking the reset link got "Auth session missing!". Root cause fully traced: the implicit auth flow puts recovery tokens in the URL hash; the `identity-mutation` Edge Function built a Supabase client with only an Authorization header — `getClaims` validates statelessly (works) but `updateUser` needs a real SESSION loaded via `setSession`, which was never called. Two-part fix: the frontend `src/lib/identityMutation.ts` now sends `access_token`+`refresh_token` in the request body, and the `identity-mutation` Edge Function calls `setSession()` before `updateUser`. The corrected Edge Function was deployed with the impersonation-gate code INLINED (no `_shared/` import — an earlier non-inlined version failed to deploy with a bundler "Module not found" error; §80 inline-divergence discipline). `src/pages/ResetPassword.tsx` was also hardened (three-state status, `onAuthStateChange` + `PASSWORD_RECOVERY` listener, `getSession` guards) — correct but not the root fix. Cole confirmed end-to-end in production. CARRYOVER: the `identity-mutation` Edge Function is NOT in the GitHub repo — deployed direct, never committed; needs a manual commit to `cbastianBWE/brainwise-blueprint` at `supabase/functions/identity-mutation/index.ts` using the inlined version. (2) **Issue 2 — coach-enrollment RPC FIXED + verified four ways (migration `enroll_path_attach_to_existing_cert_row`).** `enroll_user_in_certification_path` previously threw `user_already_has_active_certification_of_this_type` whenever a `coach_certifications` row of the same type already existed — but the coach-invite acceptance flow creates a bare cert row (no curriculum) on EVERY invite, by design, because `certification_type` drives assessment-ordering gating. That made it impossible to assign the cert path's curriculum via Learning Admin to any invited coach. The fix changes the idempotency guard from throw-always to **adopt-instead-of-throw**: if an `in_progress`/`certified` cert row of the type exists, ADOPT it (use its id, do not create a second row, do not modify it) and attach the cert path's published curricula to it, skipping any curriculum already actively assigned from `source='certification_path'` (dedup mirroring `assign_curriculum_directly` — there is no UNIQUE constraint on `user_curriculum_assignments` beyond the PK, so the dedup must be in code). The original error is preserved for the genuine-no-op case — an adopted row that already has every curriculum. Verified via impersonation-context tests as super admin: adopts an existing row (`cert_row_adopted:true`), attaches the curriculum, dedups on re-run, and still throws `user_already_has_active_certification_of_this_type` on a true duplicate. The coach-invite flow is UNTOUCHED — only the enrollment RPC changed; assessment-ordering gating is unaffected. (3) **Issue 1 — coach invite creates a bare cert row: CLOSED by decision, no fix.** The invite-acceptance flow creating a `coach_certifications` row is load-bearing — `certification_type` drives assessment-ordering gating. Fix B (decouple the invite from cert-row creation) was considered and REJECTED for exactly this reason. The bare cert row stays by design; the Issue 2 adopt-fix makes it workable. the **GUC-bypass pattern** (`app.scheduled_assignment_actor`) applied to five functions (`assign_curriculum_directly`, `assign_module_directly`, `enroll_user_in_certification_path`, `assign_mentor`, `log_super_admin_action`) so a cron context with no JWT can act — fail-closed preserved when the GUC is unset; `process_due_scheduled_assignments()` cron processor (per-row isolation); three management RPCs (`create_scheduled_assignment`, `cancel_scheduled_assignment`, `list_scheduled_assignments`); a pg_cron job `process_due_scheduled_assignments_daily` at `20 6 * * *`, active. **Part B — Excel bulk import:** a `learning-admin-imports` storage bucket (private, 10MB, xlsx/csv); `get_learning_import_reference()` RPC feeding the template's reference sheet; the `learning-admin-import` Edge Function (Class A, `verify_jwt:true`) — frontend parses xlsx with SheetJS, POSTs JSON rows, the function resolves names/emails to IDs (zero-match and ambiguous-match both fail the row), calls the bulk RPCs as the authenticated super admin, returns a per-row report. Cole verified the full bulk-import HTTP round-trip via a live UI test (one good row + one bad-email row → one succeeded, one failed). (5) **Mentor-fix RPCs SHIPPED + verified (migration `session80_v2_mentor_pair_resolution_rpcs`).** Immediate mentor assignment was broken since v1 — it passed `p_certification_id: null` and `assign_mentor` requires a real certification. Two RPCs fix it: `get_mentorable_certifications(p_mentor_user_id, p_trainee_user_id)` returns a trainee's certifications filtered to ones the mentor is qualified to mentor (qualification rule lifted verbatim from `assign_mentor`); `assign_mentor_pairs_bulk(p_mentor_user_id, p_pairs jsonb, p_reason)` takes an array of `{trainee_user_id, certification_id}` pairs, loops `assign_mentor`, per-row isolation, standard result shape. The fix prompt rebuilt the mentor assign flow to do per-trainee certification resolution: each selected trainee is resolved via `get_mentorable_certifications` — one qualifying cert auto-resolves, multiple shows a per-trainee picker, zero marks the trainee skipped — and Confirm calls `assign_mentor_pairs_bulk`. **Data finding that drove the design:** multiple certifications per person is COMMON, not rare (Cole Bastian and Test Coach 1 each hold two), so failing the multi-cert row was rejected in favour of the per-trainee picker; the picker pre-filters to certifications the selected mentor is qualified for so it never offers a pairing the RPC would reject. A trainee's certification is normally `in_progress` (a record is created at enrollment, `certified` only after completion) — `assign_mentor` requires the *mentor* to be certified but does NOT require the trainee's certification to be certified, so `in_progress` is the correct, valid state to mentor against. (b) The optional due-date field on immediate assignment accepted past dates (no frontend or backend guard) — FIXED in the fix prompt with `min={today}` on the input plus a client-side check before the RPC call. Note: the *scheduled* date was never affected — `create_scheduled_assignment` has a backend guard and was verified to reject past dates; only the separate `due_at` field lacked one. *v87 - Session 79 CLOSE — lesson_blocks trainee viewer SHIPPED end-to-end and verified. **Group W is COMPLETE** (lesson_blocks was the 8th and final content item viewer). Three backend changes + one multi-round Lovable frontend build + full live-DB verification. Two mid-session UX scope changes and one found-and-fixed pre-existing bug. (1) **Backend — three changes, all migrations applied and separately verified.** (a) Migration `add_cascade_to_complete_lesson`: added the `cascade` block (`public._compute_completion_cascade(v_caller_id, p_content_item_id)`) to `complete_lesson`'s return jsonb, bringing it in line with the six Session-78 completion RPCs (§101). (b) New RPC `get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee(p_content_item_id uuid, p_user_id uuid DEFAULT NULL)` — migration `add_get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee`. SECURITY DEFINER, access model mirrors `get_content_item_video_asset` (self with an active/completed curriculum assignment on a curriculum containing the parent module, OR mentor, OR super admin). Reuses the existing `_walk_block_config_for_asset_refs` helper. GRANT to `authenticated`+`service_role` only, anon REVOKEd. Decision settled the Session-78 open question: a parallel `_for_trainee` RPC was built rather than widening the super-admin-gated `get_lesson_block_assets` — the access models are different enough that one function with a role branch would have been less clear. (c) Migration `widen_lesson_trainee_read_policies_to_completed`: widened three RLS policies — `lesson_blocks_trainee_read`, `content_assets_trainee_read`, `content_asset_versions_trainee_read` — from `uca.status = 'active'` to `uca.status IN ('active','completed')` via in-place `ALTER POLICY` (Postgres rejects `CREATE OR REPLACE POLICY`). Required because the test trainee `+employee` is in a `completed` curriculum state; aligns these policies with `get_content_item_for_viewer`'s already-`('active','completed')` access model. (2) **New Edge Function `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` v1** — deployed `verify_jwt:false` (Class A custom auth, own `getClaims`), no `_shared/` imports so repo source and deployable source match. A JWT-bound client calls `get_lesson_block_assets_for_trainee` (the access check), then a service-role client signs the `lesson-assets` private-bucket paths. Returns `{assets:[{asset_id,signed_url,mime_type,asset_kind}],expires_in_seconds}`. Smoke-tested: no-auth → 401, OPTIONS → 200. The authenticated end-to-end signed-URL path is NOT exercised — the test lesson has no `lesson-assets` media; see test-coverage gaps below. (3) **Frontend — lesson_blocks trainee viewer SHIPPED via Lovable across multiple review rounds.** Five files at repo HEAD: `src/components/learning/viewers/LessonBlockViewer.tsx` (NEW, the paged-section viewer); `src/hooks/useLessonBlockAssets.ts` (NEW, trainee asset resolver calling the new Edge Function, the SCORM/API export seam); `src/hooks/useCompletionReporter.ts` (MODIFIED — added `reportProgress(rpcName, rpcArgs)`: a raw RPC call with no query invalidation, no cascade read, no `isReporting` flip, alongside the unchanged `reportCompletion`; the SCORM/API export seam for incremental progress); `src/pages/learning/ContentItemViewer.tsx` (MODIFIED — added `case "lesson_blocks"`, destructured/passed `reportProgress`); `src/components/super-admin/lesson-blocks/BlockRenderer.tsx` (MODIFIED — surgical edits, NOT a fork). (4) **ARCHITECTURE DECISION — Session-78 'separate renderer' decision AMENDED.** The Session-78 locked decision was a fully separate from-scratch `LessonBlockRenderer.tsx` sharing only CSS. **Overridden Session 79:** the trainee viewer REUSES the authoring `BlockRenderer.tsx` via a new `mode="trainee"` prop plus two optional props (`onBlockComplete`, `savedProgress`) that no-op in editor mode. Rationale: reuse guarantees pixel-identical trainee/authoring output and removes the visual-drift risk that a separate renderer carries; the orchestration concern that motivated the separate-renderer decision is handled by the `mode` prop and the no-op props rather than by code duplication. The authoring AI tools (`src/components/super-admin/lesson-blocks/ai-pane/`) are untouched and remain trainee-inaccessible (route guard `RoleGuard allowedRoles=["brainwise_super_admin"]` on the authoring route + super-admin-gated RPCs) — trainees correctly have no AI authoring surface. The lesson_blocks viewer has no trainee-facing AI feature in v1 (per §3.8 "no distinctive feature for v1"). (5) **§3.8 DEVIATION 1 — paged-section progression (Model B), replacing single-scroll.** The §3.8 spec describes one continuously-scrolled lesson. Cole changed this mid-session: the lesson renders ONE section at a time; Continue/Previous step linearly; the sidebar TOC jumps to ANY section (no locking — navigation is fully open); only final lesson completion is gated. Section boundaries are authored `button_stack` blocks containing an `action_type:"continue"` button — these delimiter blocks are CONSUMED (not rendered), the viewer's own Continue button replaces them. A lesson with zero continue-delimiter blocks renders as a single section (graceful fallback). The `content-item-viewer-scope.md` §3.8 text should be updated to match the shipped paged-section Model B design. (6) **§3.8 DEVIATION 2 — completion gate is `allGatedComplete && allSectionsVisited`.** The §3.8 spec gated `scroll_and_checks` mode on scroll-position-reaches-bottom. That latch-prone flag was replaced: `visitedSections` is a `Set<number>` seeded `{0}` and updated on every section change; the lesson completes only when every gating-required interactive block is complete AND every section has been visited. Furthest-position write is monotonic via a `furthestSectionRef` (the debounced `upsert_lesson_progress` early-returns when the current section index is behind the furthest; resume sets the ref to the resumed index). (7) **BUG FOUND + FIXED — match-question right-column not shuffled (pre-existing, NOT a Session-79 regression).** In `MatchTrainee` (inside `BlockRenderer.tsx`), `rightsSorted` used `[...pairs].sort((a,b)=>a.client_id…)` — a deterministic `client_id` sort, not a shuffle; with sequentially-authored `client_id`s the right column rendered in authored order, making every match question trivially solvable by row position. Pre-existing authoring-side bug, surfaced by the trainee reuse. Fixed: `rightsSorted` replaced with `useMemo(() => stableShuffle(pairs, \`${blockClientId}:${question.client_id}:match-right\`), [pairs, blockClientId, question.client_id])`; `blockClientId` threaded into `MatchTrainee` from `KnowledgeCheckRender`. The `:match-right` seed suffix avoids collision with the ranking/timeline shuffle seeds. The fix is in the shared `BlockRenderer.tsx`, so it also corrects the authoring preview. (8) **Other bugs found + fixed during the Lovable review rounds** (all corrected before close, none logged as carryover): knowledge_check completion was gated on `allCorrect` (a perfect score) — a one-way-door bug where a trainee unable to ace a check could never complete the lesson/module/cert; fixed to gate on `allAttempted` (every question Checked once, right or wrong). sessionStorage was removed from all four interactive renderers — `lesson_block_progress.completion_data` (DB) is the single source of truth; each renderer seeds in-memory `useState` lazily from a new `savedProgress` prop and a `completionFiredRef` suppresses re-firing the completion effect on already-complete blocks. Re-attempt was a no-op until the block-progress query was made attempt-scoped (`.eq("attempt_number", currentAttempt)`, `attempts_count` added to the query key, `handleReattempt` invalidates the content-item-viewer query first so `attempts_count` refreshes before the progress query re-runs). (9) **Testing — verified live against the DB.** Published test lesson: content_item `32e0e966-4cb8-4e8b-abf8-5617de346f59` ("Test Lesson Blocks Item") in Test Module C, 28 active blocks (0-27), 14 block types, `lesson_completion_mode=explicit_continue`, `is_required=false`, exactly ONE continue-delimiter `button_stack` → splits into 2 sections. Cole exercised the full UI. Backend post-run: `content_item_completions` = `completed` with `completed_at`, `lesson_furthest_continue_client_id` and `lesson_last_block_id` populated; `lesson_block_progress` attempt 1 = 6 `completed` rows all with `completion_data`, attempt 2 (re-attempt exercised) = 8 `completed` rows — attempts cleanly isolated by `attempt_number`. The celebration modal correctly did NOT fire: the content item is `is_required=false`, so completion yields only a `content_item`-tier cascade, which the chrome suppresses by design (the modal fires only for module/curriculum/certification tiers). (10) **Test-coverage gaps (carryover for future verification):** the authenticated signed-URL asset path on `get-lesson-block-asset-urls` was not run end-to-end (the test lesson has no `lesson-assets` media); the celebration modal was not run on a real module/curriculum/cert cascade (cascade plumbing on `complete_lesson` is verified by the function definition, but modal-fire on a real tier-2+ event is verified-by-design only); no `scroll_and_checks`-mode lesson fixture exists (only `explicit_continue` was tested); the mentor-role viewer path (`viewerRole === "mentor"`) is untested; the test lesson has only one section delimiter, so paging is a thin stress test. (11) **`create-checkout` integrity check (carry-forward concern):** the live function is v59 and does not use a `coach_user_id` Stripe metadata field at all (it sets `user_id`, `instrument_ids`, `checkout_type`, coach-order client fields, Pattern C comp flags). The known-fragility note about `create-checkout` losing `coach_user_id` does not apply to v59 — not a regression; the Session-79 Lovable run did not touch `supabase/functions/`. The repo copy being behind is the pre-existing v56→v59 drift (still owed — see carryover). (9) **NEW Standing rules locked Session 76:** **§99 — FK lookup tables must be audited alongside CHECK constraints when adding auditable actions.** Surfaced during quiz authoring RPC build. `super_admin_audit_log.action_type` is an FK to `super_admin_action_types`, NOT a CHECK. Every new auditable action_type must INSERT into that lookup table before the RPC succeeds. Pattern: when adding RPC that calls `log_super_admin_action(action_type=>'foo')`, audit `super_admin_action_types` for the entry, INSERT if missing in the SAME migration. Pairs with §96 (relax-RPC-validation requires matching CHECK-constraint audit). Both reinforce that validation lives at multiple layers and ALL must be touched atomically. Standing query: `SELECT * FROM super_admin_action_types WHERE action_type = 'foo';` before any new audit-emitting RPC. **§100 — Structured response shapes for client-side rendering simplification.** When a single SQL-driven response shape can produce client-side bugs around how to interpret/filter the data, refactor to a structured shape with explicit named arrays per logical role. Example from `get_quiz_for_trainee`: instead of returning a flat `options` array for match questions and forcing client to separate `display_order=0` (prompts) from `display_order=1` (answers), return `prompts` + `answers` as separate arrays. Server-side shuffle for `answers` removes need to expose `match_pair_key` to client. Net: one shape ambiguity removed, one security boundary made structural. Apply this pattern when SQL response shape forces client to make role-decisions based on data values rather than data structure. (10) **NEW Standing rules locked Session 75:** **§96 — When relaxing RPC validation, audit table-level CHECK constraints in same migration.** Lesson learned from Bug 7e/7d: `upsert_content_item` was updated to accept NULL video_source_id for supabase_storage source, but the table CHECK constraint `content_items_video_required` was missed in initial migration — required follow-up migration to relax constraint, broke first save attempt. Standing query: `SELECT pg_get_constraintdef(oid) FROM pg_constraint WHERE conrelid = 'table_name'::regclass AND contype='c';` before any RPC validation change. **§97 — Detach pattern: hard delete link rows, not soft archive.** UNIQUE constraints `(certification_path_id, curriculum_id)` and `(curriculum_id, module_id)` would block reattach if soft-deleted via archived_at. User enrollments preserved (Option A locked Session 75) by NOT cascading detach to user_curriculum_assignments / user_module_assignments. Clear sibling prerequisite_*_id references first in detach RPC to avoid FK violations. **§98 — Duplicate pattern: deep copy with assets SHARED by reference, new entities start unpublished.** Storage-efficient (same asset bytes referenced by multiple content_items). New entities `is_published=false` forces author review before exposure. Slug + name editable in dialog. Internal helper RPCs `_duplicate_module_children(p_source_module_id, p_target_module_id, p_caller_id)` and `_duplicate_curriculum_full(p_source_curriculum_id, p_new_slug, p_new_name, p_caller_id)` reusable, not exposed via grant. Use jsonb map (object, not array) to track source_id → target_id for cross-reference resolution within the same duplicate transaction. (11) **Sequencing decision for Session 76:** Two valid paths.
