*v81 - Session 73 CLOSE (security audit cycle) — Full Lovable security scan cycle run after Pattern C shipped. Initial scan surfaced 2 errors + 9 warnings. Four diagnostic rounds with Lovable to triage every finding into real bug vs scanner cache vs design-intentional. Outcome: 7 backend migrations + 2 Edge Function deploys + 2 GitHub commits + 2 Lovable frontend prompts shipped to close every real bug; all false positives + design-intentional warnings marked as ignored in Lovable UI with documented rationale. Final scanner state: 0 errors, 0 warnings, 15 items in Ignored. (1) **Migration `security_session_73_error_1_drop_trainee_writes_and_82_sweep` SHIPPED.** Closed Error 1 ("Quiz Scores Manipulation"). Dropped trainee-direct UPDATE/INSERT policies on `content_item_completions`, `lesson_block_progress`, `quiz_attempts`, `written_submissions`. All writes now flow exclusively through 11 SECURITY DEFINER RPCs (`record_video_progress`, `confirm_external_link`, `submit_file_upload`, `mark_live_event_attendance`, `upsert_lesson_progress`, `upsert_lesson_block_progress`, `start_lesson_reattempt`, `complete_lesson`, plus the 3 written-submission/quiz-attempt RPCs from prior sessions). Trainees can no longer write arbitrary values; the RPCs validate and stamp the proper fields. §82 sweep on surviving policies on these tables — explicit `TO authenticated`/`TO service_role` declarations everywhere. (2) **Migration `security_session_73_error_2_lock_account_type_org_id_practitioner_flag` SHIPPED.** Closed Error 2 ("Super admin role escalation"). Rewrote `enforce_immutable_user_fields()` trigger to freeze `account_type`, `organization_id`, AND `is_practitioner_coach` (added Session 73 Pattern C) for ALL callers EXCEPT `brainwise_super_admin`. Bypass paths: super admin (legitimate elevation/promotion path), the existing GUC opt-out `app.bypass_user_immutable_check` (used by `invitation_redeem`), and `auth.uid() IS NULL` (system trigger paths). Verified: company_admin attempting UPDATE on their own row to set `account_type='corporate_employee'` raises permission denied; full_name updates still succeed. The trigger now covers all three privilege-bearing columns; prior version only covered `account_type` + `organization_id`. (3) **Migration `security_session_73_quiz_questions_82_anti_pattern_fix` SHIPPED.** §82 sweep on `quiz_questions` + `quiz_answer_options` policies. Both tables had `roles: {public}` defaulted-in on service_role policies (the exact §82 anti-pattern). DROP+CREATE all affected policies with explicit `TO service_role`. (4) **Migration `security_session_73_coach_clients_client_view_complete_columns` SHIPPED.** Closed the real bug behind Lovable's "Clients Can Read Coaches' Private Notes" finding. Rewrote the existing `coach_clients_client_view` view with 16 client-safe columns + `WHERE client_user_id = auth.uid()` gate. Explicitly EXCLUDES `coach_notes` (the leak vector), all Stripe fields (`stripe_payment_intent_id`, `stripe_session_id`, `stripe_customer_id`, etc.), refund/coupon/revoked/source columns. The view's WHERE clause IS the gate — security_definer (NOT security_invoker) was chosen because base-table policy must remain locked (see Migration 6 below). (5) **Migration `security_session_73_coach_clients_view_revoke_extra_grants` SHIPPED.** Revoked INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE/TRUNCATE from authenticated on `coach_clients_client_view`. Kept SELECT. Tightens defense-in-depth: even if base-table writability were ever accidentally added to the view by Postgres view-update rules, the explicit revoke prevents misuse. (6) **Migration `security_session_73_drop_coach_clients_leaky_client_select_policy` SHIPPED.** DROPPED the `coach_clients: clients read their own invitation` policy. This was the original leak — the policy gated SELECT on `client_user_id = auth.uid()` but applied to ALL columns including `coach_notes`. Removal means clients have NO direct base-table SELECT on `coach_clients`. All client reads route through `coach_clients_client_view` (Migration 4) which projects only the 16 safe columns. (7) **Migration `security_session_73_cohorts_82_anti_pattern_fix` SHIPPED.** §82 sweep on `cohorts` + `cohort_members` super_admin policies (same anti-pattern: `roles: {public}` defaulted-in). DROP+CREATE clean. Both tables empty in production today (Phase 5 / Group D feature not built yet); fix is forward-looking — when the cohorts feature ships, policies are already clean. (8) **Edge Function `create-checkout` v55→v56 deployed (verify_jwt:true, ACTIVE).** Three hardening additions, all preserved byte-identical from Pattern C v55 except the new validations: `PRICE_ID_ALLOWLIST = new Set<string>([5 Stripe price IDs matching src/lib/stripe.ts exactly])` validated at line 84 — rejects unknown price_ids with 400 `price_id_not_allowed` before Stripe session creation. `ALLOWED_ORIGINS` Set + `LOVABLE_PREVIEW_PATTERN` regex + `isOriginAllowed()` helper at lines 22-40 — validates Origin header before constructing `safeOrigin` used in `success_url`/`cancel_url`, returns 400 `origin_not_allowed` if mismatch. `MAX_QUANTITY = 50` enforced at line 95 — rejects out-of-bounds quantity with 400. Pattern C comp coupon logic (`get_applicable_comp_coupon` lookup + `discounts:[{coupon}]` injection + `metadata.bw_super_admin_comp` stamping) preserved verbatim. The `req.headers.get("origin") || "http://localhost:3000"` fallback the scanner flagged was removed entirely. (9) **Edge Function `customer-portal` v40→v41 deployed (verify_jwt:true, ACTIVE).** Same Origin allowlist hardening pattern applied to `return_url` construction at lines 21-37 + 63-71. Returns 400 `origin_not_allowed` before any `safeOrigin` value reaches Stripe `return_url`. (10) **GitHub commits SHIPPED Session 73 close.** Both deployed Edge Functions sync'd to repo `main`: `supabase/functions/create-checkout/index.ts` (deployed v56 source replaces prior repo version that was already drifted from runtime before Pattern C) and `supabase/functions/customer-portal/index.ts` (deployed v41 source). Resolves repo↔runtime drift discovered Round 2 of the audit when Lovable's scanner found references to lines that didn't exist in the deployed version. Cole uploaded manually via GitHub web UI (READ-ONLY MCP). Standing rule reinforced: **whenever an Edge Function is deployed via Supabase MCP, the same source MUST be uploaded to GitHub same-session to keep repo↔runtime in sync.** Pre-existing drift on these two files predated Session 73 (Pattern C v55 deploy was the first MCP deploy on `create-checkout`; the repo version dated from earlier Lovable-shipped versions). Going forward: every deploy commits same session. (11) **Lovable prompt `coach_clients_client_view` frontend swap SHIPPED.** Five client-side `.from("coach_clients")` queries swapped to `.from("coach_clients_client_view")` across 4 files: `src/pages/MyResults.tsx` (2 calls at lines ~437 + 454), `src/pages/Onboarding.tsx` (1 call at line ~42), `src/pages/PrivacySettings.tsx` (1 call at line ~116), `src/components/assessment/InstrumentSelection.tsx` (2 calls at lines ~95 + 104). Coach-side queries on `coach_clients` base table (e.g., `src/pages/coach/CoachClients.tsx`) left untouched — coaches still need full table access including their own `coach_notes`. Verified Onboarding.tsx and PrivacySettings.tsx via GitHub `get_file_contents` after Lovable ship. (12) **Lovable prompt `ai-chat + generate-report` rate limit + length cap SHIPPED.** Two Edge Function source changes in `supabase/functions/`: (a) `ai-chat/index.ts` lines 70-83 — `message.length > 4000` → HTTP 400 `message_too_long`; `conversation_history.length > 50` → HTTP 400 `conversation_history_too_long`. Pre-Anthropic-call validation prevents oversized payloads from consuming credits. (b) `generate-report/index.ts` lines 70-94 — pre-Anthropic-call rate limit via `check-ai-usage` Edge Function with `usage_type: "report_generation"`, gated by `!isInternal` so internal-secret callers (`retry-ptp-narratives`) bypass intentionally. Returns 429 when quota exceeded. Verified both in GitHub main after Lovable deploy. (13) **All security findings dispositioned (15 items total, final scanner state clean):** REAL BUGS CLOSED (5): Error 1 quiz scores manipulation (Migration 1), Error 2 super admin escalation (Migration 2), coach_notes exposure to clients (Migrations 4+5+6 + Lovable view swap), Stripe price_id not validated (Edge Function v56), Stripe redirect URLs from unvalidated origin (Edge Function v56 + v41), generate-report no rate limiting (Lovable ai-chat/generate-report prompt), ai-chat unbounded message size (Lovable ai-chat/generate-report prompt). SCANNER CACHE / FALSE POSITIVES (Lovable scanner stale snapshot after fixes shipped, marked ignored with rationale): Stripe price_id, Stripe redirect URLs, ai-chat unbounded, generate-report no rate limit, coach_clients leaky policy (all already fixed but scanner didn't re-evaluate). DESIGN-INTENTIONAL (marked ignored): Trainees cannot read lesson-assets storage directly (§84 design — signed URLs via `get_lesson_block_assets` RPC are the canonical access path), Coaches cannot read `coach_pending_bulk_batches` directly (Session 71 design — webhook reconstruction mechanism, coaches see status via `coach_clients` grouped by `stripe_payment_intent_id`), `lesson-thumbnails` bucket allows public SELECT (§84 design — public-tier promotional imagery), `coach_clients_client_view` is SECURITY DEFINER (intentional — view's WHERE clause is the gate, security_invoker would require re-adding the leaky base-table policy). DEFERRED-BY-DESIGN (logged forward, marked ignored): Cohort members cannot read cohort records (Phase 5/Group D feature not yet built, RLS already drafted clean), Lesson assets inaccessible to enrolled trainees from storage (same as §84 design pattern above), 95 SECURITY DEFINER functions with anon EXECUTE (Session 71 deferred to dedicated audit session, no live exploit because all 77 Edge Functions use service role). (14) **Build Queue items added Session 73 security audit cycle:** (a) **Post-launch refactor: replace `coach_clients_client_view` with SECURITY DEFINER RPC `get_my_coach_invitations()`.** Views with implicit security_definer behavior + WHERE-clause-as-gate work correctly but are slightly fragile to future Postgres version semantics; converting to an explicit SECURITY DEFINER RPC with documented auth check is cleaner long-term. Low priority because current view works correctly. (b) **Session 71 anon EXECUTE audit on 95 SECDEF functions.** Dedicated audit session walking each function with anon EXECUTE and deciding per-function: keep (signup/public probe), `SECURITY INVOKER` (RLS handles it), or `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM anon, PUBLIC`. No live exploit (all Edge Functions use service role); defense-in-depth concern only. Lovable's auto-fix path would likely break signup/auth flows by over-revoking — must be hand-walked. (c) **Phase 5/Group D cohort SELECT policy for enrolled members.** When cohorts feature ships, add `cohort_members can read their own cohorts` policy (currently empty tables, just service_role + super_admin policies live). (d) **Stripe `price_id` / origin pattern lessons learned doc.** Add to architecture-reference: when shipping new Edge Functions that consume external request data (Stripe API, third-party webhooks, etc.), the allowlist pattern (`new Set([known_values])` + `helperFn()` validator + 400 reject before downstream call) is the standing pattern. Already applied to `create-checkout` v56 and `customer-portal` v41 — formalize as §91 in architecture-reference next session. (e) **Repo↔runtime sync discipline.** Every Supabase MCP `deploy_edge_function` MUST be followed same-session by GitHub commit of the deployed source. Pre-Session-73 drift on `create-checkout` and `customer-portal` cost ~30 minutes of Round 2 audit time to diagnose. Going forward, drift is preventable. (15) **Standing patterns from Session 73 security audit:** **Diagnostic rounds with Lovable as triage tool.** When a scanner produces N findings, the cost-efficient pattern is: Round 1 — send all findings to Lovable with explicit "diagnose only, do not write code" instruction; Lovable reports back which are real and which are scanner cache. Round 2 — Claude verifies the real ones via Supabase MCP queries + GitHub `get_file_contents`. Round 3 — fix migrations + Edge Function deploys ship for real bugs. Round 4 — re-run scanner, expect cache + lingering false positives, batch-ignore with documented rationale. Four rounds beats four sequential fix-then-rescan cycles. **View-as-gate pattern for column-level privacy on row-readable tables.** When a base table has rows that some viewers should see SOME columns of but not OTHERS, and direct base-table SELECT gating cannot project columns, the canonical pattern is: (a) drop the base-table SELECT policy for the limited-access viewer class, (b) create a SECURITY DEFINER view that projects only safe columns + WHERE clause filtering to the viewer's authorized rows, (c) revoke non-SELECT grants from authenticated on the view, (d) frontend reads through the view exclusively. Applied Session 73 to `coach_clients_client_view`. **Two-stage RLS audit pattern.** Stage 1 quick query: `SELECT tablename, policyname, roles FROM pg_policies WHERE schemaname='public' AND 'public'=ANY(roles) AND qual='true';` Surfaces every §82 anti-pattern in one query. Stage 2 per-table audit: read all policies on each high-value table (assessments, results, coach_clients, user-PII-bearing tables) and check explicit `TO role` + non-trivial qual. Stage 1 catches the common case; Stage 2 catches the subtle case. Edge Function versions at Session 73 close UPDATED for security audit: `create-checkout` v56 ACTIVE verify_jwt:true (Pattern C + security hardening), `customer-portal` v41 ACTIVE verify_jwt:true (security hardening), `create-comp-coupon` v2 ACTIVE verify_jwt:false (Pattern C, unchanged), `stripe-webhook` v26 ACTIVE verify_jwt:false (Pattern C, unchanged), `ai-chat` + `generate-report` latest Lovable deploys with new validation logic.*



*v80 - Session 73 CLOSE — Pattern C "super admin acts as practitioner coach" SHIPPED end-to-end. Standalone one-off session. Eight backend migrations + three Edge Function deploys + one Lovable prompt (6 files) + one hotfix migration + one synthetic data row. Verified live with two successful comp-paid coach invitations from super admin to test client emails — Stripe Checkout bypassed entirely (frontend short-circuits to direct DB write + email send when the comp coupon system has an applicable 100% coupon for the caller), invitation emails delivered, no real money charged, test client invitations exist in `coach_clients` ready for the clients to sign up and take their PTP assessments at $0. The frontend route guards, sidebar Coach Tools section, and `/super-admin/coupons` admin page all working as designed. One pre-existing frontend bug discovered and hotfixed in same session (My Clients roster table not filtering revoked invitations). (1) **Migration A `pattern_c_a_comp_coupons_table` SHIPPED.** New `comp_coupons` table for managing Stripe-side promotional/comp coupons via BrainWise admin UI. Columns: id, stripe_coupon_id (UNIQUE), internal_name, description, percent_off (1-100 CHECK), duration (once/repeating/forever CHECK), duration_in_months (conditional CHECK — required when repeating, must be null otherwise), max_redemptions, redeem_by (NOT NULL — every coupon expires), applicable_account_types text[], applicable_instrument_ids uuid[], created_by FK users(id), created_at, archived_at, archive_reason, notes. 4 indexes including partial `idx_comp_coupons_active WHERE archived_at IS NULL`. 2 §82-clean RLS policies (super_admin ALL TO authenticated with role gate, service_role ALL). The applicable_account_types and applicable_instrument_ids arrays default null meaning "any" — Pattern C super_admin_comp coupon uses `['brainwise_super_admin']` for account type and null for instruments (applies to all 4). (2) **Migration B `pattern_c_b_comp_coupon_rpcs_and_action_types` SHIPPED.** Two action_type whitelist rows added to `super_admin_action_types`: `comp_coupon_created` and `comp_coupon_archived` — both category=content_authoring (initial assignment), requires_mfa=false, requires_justification=true, denylist_during_impersonation=true. Three RPCs deployed: `_insert_comp_coupon_row` (internal, SECURITY DEFINER, 13-param, service-role-only EXECUTE initially per defense-in-depth — see B3 for the hotfix), `get_applicable_comp_coupon(p_caller_user_id, p_instrument_id)` (SECURITY DEFINER STABLE, returns TABLE shape with out_coupon_id/out_stripe_coupon_id/out_internal_name/out_percent_off, filters by archived_at IS NULL + redeem_by > now() + account_type match + instrument match if specified, ORDER BY percent_off DESC then created_at DESC for tiebreak, LIMIT 1), `archive_comp_coupon(p_coupon_id, p_reason)` (super-admin-gated via assert_super_admin + impersonation gate, reason min 10 chars, soft-deletes via archived_at + archive_reason, does NOT delete Stripe-side coupon). (3) **Migration B2 `pattern_c_b2_add_impersonation_gate_to_insert_comp_coupon_row` SHIPPED.** Added `PERFORM public.assert_impersonation_allows('financial_transaction')` to `_insert_comp_coupon_row` after the super-admin check. Rationale: keep impersonation enforcement at the DB layer rather than in the Edge Function, avoiding the `_shared/impersonation_gate.ts` sync gap with GitHub repo (file lives in deployed runtime only, not in repo). The gate fires regardless of how the RPC is reached. financial_transaction is in the impersonation denylist — coupon creation can't happen during any impersonation session even in act mode. (4) **Migration C `pattern_c_c_is_practitioner_coach_column` SHIPPED.** New `users.is_practitioner_coach boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false` column. Partial index `idx_users_is_practitioner_coach WHERE is_practitioner_coach = true`. Backfilled all `account_type IN ('coach', 'brainwise_super_admin')` rows to true. Verified: 5 of 5 coaches flagged, 2 of 2 super admins flagged, 0 leaks to other account types. Decouples "what is your primary account type" from "do you provide coaching services" — a brainwise_super_admin can simultaneously be a practitioner coach (Pattern C) without sharing the super admin's elevated permissions across role boundaries. The 2 super admin users both got the flag automatically per Lock 5; if the second super admin is not supposed to be a practitioner coach, manual UPDATE to false is the deliberate action (flagged for Cole's awareness). (5) **Migration D `pattern_c_d_current_user_is_practitioner_coach_helper` SHIPPED.** New `current_user_is_practitioner_coach()` SECURITY DEFINER STABLE function returning boolean. Mirrors the existing `current_user_account_type()` pattern. Returns COALESCE of users.is_practitioner_coach for auth.uid(), or false. Used inside RLS policies on coach-affordance tables so policies don't need inline subqueries against users. EXECUTE granted to authenticated + service_role. (6) **Migration E `pattern_c_e_swap_coach_rls_to_practitioner_flag` SHIPPED.** 7 RLS policies on coach-affordance tables DROP+CREATE swapped from `current_user_account_type()='coach'` to `current_user_is_practitioner_coach() = true`. Tables: `users` (coaches can read their clients), `assessments` (coaches read client assessments), `assessment_responses` (coaches read client responses), `assessment_results` (coaches read client results), `assessment_acknowledgments` (coaches read client acks), `facet_interpretations` (coaches read client interpretations), `coach_disclosure_acceptances` (coach inserts own). All 7 recreated §82-clean with explicit `TO authenticated`. Backfill from Migration C means all real coaches already have the flag true, so this swap is behavior-preserving for them. New behavior: super admin practitioner coaches now pass these policies and can see clients/assessments/results for the coach_clients rows where coach_user_id = their UUID. Pre-existing observation logged: 3 OTHER policies on `coach_disclosure_acceptances` still carry `roles: {public}` (the coach-reads-own SELECT, the service_role ALL, and the super-admin-reads-all SELECT) — these are §82 anti-pattern leftovers from pre-Session-71 work that didn't get caught in the security audit sweep. Logged as a Build Queue item for the next §82 audit pass; low severity because the policies' quals are scoped (auth.uid()/role check inside qual), not blanket TRUE. (7) **Migration F `pattern_c_f_coach_shareable_link_rpcs_practitioner_widening` SHIPPED.** Both `coach_shareable_link_coach_paid` and `coach_shareable_link_self_pay` PL/pgSQL RPCs reworked. Auth gate widened: accepts `account_type='coach'` OR `(account_type='brainwise_super_admin' AND is_practitioner_coach=true)`. Cert check bypassed entirely for super admin practitioner coaches per Lock 5 (Cole's explicit instruction "we are not gated by being certified"). For super admin practitioner coaches, allowed_instrument_ids = all 4 instruments (PTP/NAI/AIRSA/HSS). Real coach path completely unchanged (cert check still required, allowed instruments still derived from certification_type IN ('ptp_coach', 'ai_transformation_coach', 'ai_transformation_ptp_coach', 'my_brainwise_coach')). All other RPC logic preserved verbatim — email validation, name trimming, instrument validation, pricing lookup, batch row construction, FOREACH insert loop. (8) **Migration G `pattern_c_g_practitioner_coach_sync_trigger` SHIPPED.** New `_sync_is_practitioner_coach_on_account_type()` SECURITY DEFINER trigger function + 2 BEFORE triggers on users table. INSERT trigger fires when `NEW.account_type IN ('coach', 'brainwise_super_admin')`. UPDATE trigger fires when `NEW.account_type IN (...) AND OLD.account_type IS DISTINCT FROM NEW.account_type`. Auto-flips `is_practitioner_coach=true` only when transition INTO the target role happens. Does NOT auto-flip OFF when account_type transitions away — that's a permission-removal action and must be deliberate (manual UPDATE), not implicit. Found during Migration G design: `handle_new_user` trigger does NOT set `account_type` (only handles ToS/Privacy version capture + email/full_name), so a trigger fired on auth.users insert wouldn't have account_type to read. The right hook is on public.users UPDATE OF account_type. Verified via DO-block test inside transaction-with-cleanup (flipped a test individual user to coach, checked flag went true, restored). (9) **Edge Function `create-comp-coupon` v1→v2 ACTIVE, verify_jwt:false.** Initial v1 deploy used Class A custom auth (auth.getClaims) + super_admin gate + Stripe API call + RPC call via service-role client. v1 had a critical bug discovered during Cole's first attempt to create the super_admin_comp coupon: the `_insert_comp_coupon_row` RPC's internal call to `log_super_admin_action` reads `auth.uid()`, which is NULL when invoked by service-role. The audit log function raised `Authentication required` and the whole transaction rolled back, causing the Edge Function to return 500 with `db_insert_failed`. Diagnosis took 3 minutes: zero rows in `super_admin_audit_log` for `comp_coupon_created` in the failure window meant the failure happened BEFORE audit logging, narrowing to either auth/validation OR the Stripe step OR DB insert. Synthetic test call to `_insert_comp_coupon_row` directly from MCP execute_sql raised the exact `Authentication required: log_super_admin_action cannot be called without an authenticated session` error, conclusively isolating the bug. **Hotfix Migration B3 `pattern_c_b3_grant_insert_comp_coupon_row_to_authenticated` SHIPPED.** Granted EXECUTE on `_insert_comp_coupon_row` to `authenticated` role (the internal super-admin gate inside the RPC body still protects it from non-super-admin callers — defense in depth). **Edge Function v2 deployed.** Switched the RPC call from `serviceClient` to `callerClient` (which carries the caller's JWT). Now `auth.uid()` resolves to Cole's super admin UUID inside `log_super_admin_action`, audit attribution is to the human actor not service role, transaction commits cleanly. Side benefit: cleaner audit trail. After v2 deploy, Cole's coupon creation succeeded on first retry. Standing pattern lesson: any SECURITY DEFINER RPC that internally calls `log_super_admin_action` (or any other auth.uid()-dependent function) MUST be invoked via a JWT-bearing client, not service role. The Edge Function pattern in this codebase historically defaulted to service-role for cross-cutting RPC calls; the new pattern is caller-JWT for any RPC that audits. (10) **Edge Function `create-checkout` v54→v55 ACTIVE, verify_jwt:true.** Surgical edit adding `get_applicable_comp_coupon(user.id, null)` lookup before building Stripe session params. If a coupon row is returned, adds `discounts: [{ coupon: stripe_coupon_id }]` to sessionParams AND stamps `metadata.bw_super_admin_comp: "true"` + `metadata.bw_comp_coupon_internal_name: <name>` on the session metadata. The instrument_id parameter passed as null (option 1 of three discussed) means the coupon applies session-wide — Stripe coupons apply to whole sessions anyway, so a single-instrument-restricted coupon doesn't fit Stripe's model. Future per-instrument promotions would need a different lookup strategy (loop per instrument and pick best) but Pattern C launch doesn't need that. ALL existing flow preserved verbatim — auth lookup, Stripe customer find-or-create, line_items, success_url/cancel_url, all existing metadata keys (user_id, instrument_ids, checkout_type, client_email/first_name/last_name/coach_note for coach_order mode). The lookup is wrapped in try/catch so a coupon RPC error doesn't block checkout — best-effort augmentation, real coach flows unchanged when no coupon matches their account_type. (11) **Edge Function `stripe-webhook` v25→v26 ACTIVE, verify_jwt:false.** Surgical edits in BOTH `coach_order` (single-client) AND `coach_bulk_order` (Group D) branches. Read `metadata.bw_super_admin_comp === "true"` into `isSuperAdminComp` boolean at the top of `checkout.session.completed` handler. Guard `recalculateCombinedCouponForEmail` calls with `if (!isSuperAdminComp)` — skip the client-facing credit-coupon generation on $0 super-admin comp orders (no money to credit back to client). Real coach orders ALWAYS run `recalculateCombinedCouponForEmail` unchanged because `bw_super_admin_comp` metadata is never set on their sessions. All other webhook logic preserved verbatim: coach_clients insertion, assessment_purchases insertion, sendInvitationEmail (fires unconditionally on both paths — preserves Cole's hard constraint "invitation stuff stays intact"), bulk batch completion stamping, subscription tier handling. The bw_super_admin_comp metadata key is purpose-built (not a generic "comp applied" signal) so future promotional coupons for real coaches won't accidentally trigger the credit-skip behavior. (12) **Migration H `pattern_c_h_synthetic_my_brainwise_coach_cert_for_super_admin` SHIPPED.** Synthetic `coach_certifications` row inserted for Cole's super admin user: `certification_type='my_brainwise_coach'`, `status='certified'`, `enrolled_by` + `certified_by` both = Cole's UUID (self-attested), `free_assessment_uses` = `[]::jsonb`, `notes` flag the row as synthetic for future maintainers ("Pattern C synthetic certification (Session 73). Super admin acting as practitioner coach. NOT a real cert path completion. Use users.is_practitioner_coach + users.account_type to identify Pattern C super admins; do not count this row in real-coach analytics."). Discovered during end-to-end testing: the My Clients page disables the Order Assessment button when `coach_certifications` is empty for the user, regardless of `is_practitioner_coach`. Frontend cert check is separate from the RPC cert check (which Migration F already widened to bypass for super admin practitioner coaches). Two fix options considered: (A) frontend fix to teach order-button enable logic to pass for super admin practitioner coaches — clean architecturally but requires Lovable round-trip and finding every cert-check location across the FE; (B) backend fix giving Cole a synthetic certification row — single SQL insert, no frontend changes, slight pollution of coach_certifications table. *v78 - Session 71 CLOSE — Security audit session. Seven findings surfaced (one ERROR + six WARN-class via the Supabase advisor and Lovable's security scanner); five shipped this session, two deferred with documented rationale. Final advisor state at session close: 304 lints, ZERO ERROR, all WARN. No Group C feature work this session. Sessions 70 (Phase 5/9 backend + Resource Authoring UI) and the one-off D-series session (Your Assessment Responses 2+/2- + coach-client split-pair fixes) are the prior entries below. Session 72 opens on the Group C completion sequence; see `group-c-completion-sequence.md` for the locked order and `phase-5-9-scope-delta.md` for the remaining 5/9 frontend work. (1) **Finding 1 — 27 tables with anon-readable `roles: {public}` policies SHIPPED FIXED.** Every `service role full access` policy on the Group C / notifications tables had been created with `qual: 'true'` and no explicit `TO service_role`, defaulting `roles` to `{public}`. Postgres OR's RLS policies, so one permissive `USING (true) WITH CHECK (true)` policy beat every restrictive one. Anon SET LOCAL probe live-confirmed exposure: 41 rows from `impersonation_sessions`, 57 from `super_admin_action_types`, 17 from `notification_types_catalog`, 12 from `assessment_acknowledgments` (PII), 4 from `user_notifications` (PII), plus smaller exposures across 22 more tables. Migration `security_audit_round1_findings_1_2_3` dropped + recreated each policy `FOR ALL TO service_role`. Tables touched (27): assessment_acknowledgments, certification_path_curricula, certification_paths, coach_disclosure_acceptances, coach_disclosure_versions, coach_mentor_assignments, cohort_members, cohorts, content_item_completions, content_items, curricula, curriculum_modules, impersonation_sessions, lesson_block_progress, module_completions, modules, notification_types_catalog, quiz_answer_options, quiz_attempts, quiz_questions, resource_access_grants, resource_tabs, super_admin_action_types, user_curriculum_assignments, user_notification_preferences, user_notifications, written_submissions. (2) **Finding 1b — 4 published-content policies also `roles: {public}` SHIPPED FIXED.** During Finding 1 verification, discovered four `authenticated read published` policies on `content_items`, `curricula`, `curriculum_modules`, `modules` also had `roles: {public}` so anon could SELECT published curriculum (3+1+3+1 rows leaked). Migration `security_audit_finding_1b_published_content_anon_leak` dropped+recreated `FOR SELECT TO authenticated`. (3) **Finding 2 — `org_users_public` view SECURITY DEFINER SHIPPED FIXED.** Pre-existing Supabase advisor ERROR-class warning. View had `security_invoker=false` explicitly. Verified zero in-codebase consumers via Lovable grep (only types.ts generator noise). `ALTER VIEW ... SET (security_invoker=true)` bundled in the Finding 1 migration. (4) **Finding 3 — 7 SECURITY INVOKER functions with mutable search_path SHIPPED FIXED.** `airsa_skills_set_updated_at`, `_ai_authoring_conversations_touch_updated_at`, `_asset_kind_size_ceiling`, `_asset_kind_mime_allowed`, `_asset_extract_ext`, `_asset_active_ref_count`, `impersonation_denylist_categories`. `ALTER FUNCTION ... SET search_path = public, pg_temp` for each, bundled in the Finding 1 migration. (5) **Finding 6 — per-instrument visibility model gaps SHIPPED FIXED** (after product Q&A and Lovable diagnostic round 3.5). The docs say PTP is shareable via toggles, AIRSA is dual-rater-visible to supervisors and admins, NAI and HSS are individual-only. The RLS on `assessments`, `assessment_acknowledgments`, `assessment_results`, and `assessment_responses` was instrument-blind for the corporate-admin, coach, and permission-gated org paths. Lovable's deep dive corrected the initial framing — `assessment_results` is instrument-blind for two paths (coach + permission-gated org admin), so scores leak through those paths too, not just metadata. Cole's product answers locked Session 71: Q1 = B (completion metadata fair game for admins, no change to admin policies on assessments/acks). Q2 = single-toggle PTP-only PrivacySettings UI confirmed (defense-in-depth: add `instrument_id='INST-001'` to the permission-gated org access policy). Q3 = A (coach RLS stays instrument-blind, upstream gating via CERT_TYPE_TO_INSTRUMENTS in CoachClients.tsx is sufficient). Q4 = supervisor AIRSA metadata visibility is acceptable (nice-to-have, add a supervisor-AIRSA policy on `assessments` so future supervisor UIs that query parent metadata just work). Migration `security_audit_finding_6_per_instrument_visibility` (round 3.5 — after Lovable caught that the inline `SELECT id FROM users WHERE supervisor_user_id=auth.uid()` subquery returns nothing for non-admin supervisors because `users` RLS only gives them `users: read own row`): two changes, one transaction. Change 1: dropped and recreated `assessment_results: permission-gated org access` with `instrument_id='INST-001'` AND `current_user_account_type() = ANY(ARRAY['company_admin','org_admin','brainwise_super_admin'])` AT TOP LEVEL (planner short-circuits per Lovable's cosmetic recommendation) before the EXISTS-against-permissions. Change 2: new policy `assessments: supervisors read direct reports AIRSA` using the existing `public.get_my_direct_reports()` SECURITY DEFINER STABLE helper (search_path=public already pinned, already filters `deactivated_at IS NULL` on reports). Verified via simulated JWT for `a1d4fc3f-d635-49ae-96d4-81b0e64864c6` (demo-csuite-1 in Test Corp, supervises 2 reports): supervisor sees 9 INST-003 rows (3 self+manager rows × 2 reports = correct), zero INST-001/INST-002/INST-004 rows for those reports. Working as designed. (6) **Finding 7 — `ai-authoring-temp` storage bucket anon-readable SHIPPED FIXED.** Caught by Lovable's security scanner re-scan post-Finding-1 (not surfaced by Supabase advisor because the advisor doesn't lint Storage policies). `ai_authoring_temp_service_role_all` policy on `storage.objects` had `roles: {public}` and qual only checked `bucket_id` — same exact anti-pattern as Finding 1, just on Storage. Anon could SELECT every object's row in the AI-authoring temp bucket (1 object visible to anon at session start — a real `MODULE 1 - Bias.docx` Cole had uploaded). (7) **Finding 4 — 95 SECURITY DEFINER functions with anon EXECUTE — DEFERRED to its own audit session.** 207 SECDEF functions total, 95 anon-executable including admin-grade ones (`grant_certification`, `log_super_admin_action`, `export_audit_events`, etc.). No live exploit because all 77 edge functions use service role (verified via list_edge_functions — none use the anon key). Defense-in-depth concern only. Lovable's auto-fix would likely break signup/auth flows by over-revoking. Tagged for a dedicated audit session that walks each function with anon EXECUTE and decides per-function: keep (signup/public probe), `SECURITY INVOKER` (RLS handles it), or `REVOKE EXECUTE FROM anon, PUBLIC`. "Enrolled trainees cannot read lesson assets from storage" = defer; the signed-URL path via `get_lesson_block_assets` RPC bypasses RLS for trainee asset reads, no direct storage.objects access from trainee. (6) **RECURRING LESSON — extending a pre-existing table needs a FULL audit of defaults + CHECK constraints + RLS policies, not just ADD COLUMN.** Extending `resources` caused FOUR separate bugs this session, all the same root: `phase9_b2` (legacy NOT-NULL columns blocked inserts), `phase9_e2b` (explicit null overrode a column default), `phase9_b3` (RLS gap), plus the content_type CHECK guess caught pre-build. Greenfield tables (`module_completions`) didn't have this hazard. Standing rule: before extending an established table, audit its full DDL — `\d+`, `pg_get_constraintdef` for CHECKs, `pg_policies` for RLS. (7) Tooling-capability lesson: Claude CAN read/write Postgres functions via `pg_get_functiondef`+`execute_sql` (they live in the DB), CAN write Edge Functions via `deploy_edge_function`, CANNOT read the deployed Edge Function runtime (this session's MCP had no `get_edge_function`). When an Edge Function has uncommitted `_shared/` deps, ask Cole for the Dashboard Download-button bundle up front. *v75 - Session 69 CLOSE — All four interactive block types SHIPPED end-to-end (flashcards from Session 67/68, card_sort + scenario + knowledge_check shipped this session) plus four backend hot-fixes resolving AI Refine bugs across all interactive types. (1) Lovable prompts shipped serially per §75: card_sort (session-69-card-sort.md, 1462 lines, verified working with PTP True/False example), scenario (session-70-scenario.md, 1401 lines, shipped after stripping markdown formatting to fit Lovable's ~48k input cap), knowledge_check 4a (session-71, 44,629 chars — adds block + MC + multi_select + true_false), knowledge_check 4b (session-72, 28,408 chars — adds fill_in_blank + match), knowledge_check 4c (session-73, 33,417 chars — adds ranking + timeline). User confirmed "all three prompts worked" on knowledge_check sub-prompts. (2) Edge Function hot-fix progression — draft-lesson-block v12→v13→v14→v15 + expand-lesson-from-outline v11→v12→v13. **v12→v13:** MAX_OUTPUT_TOKENS raised 3000→8000 (matches scaffold-lesson v6 and expand-lesson-from-outline v11). Root cause: 10-moment scenario refines (and other high-density generates like 5-question knowledge_check or 20-card flashcards) easily exceed 3000 output tokens; Anthropic returned max_tokens-truncated JSON; JSON.parse threw; 502 ai_output_unparseable. 3000 was sized for single-instruction refines on simple blocks (text, heading); interactive blocks were added Sessions 65-66 without re-tuning the cap. **v13→v14 + v11→v12 parity:** Added explicit "EVERY markdown-typed field MUST be populated with non-empty Markdown STRING" directive to system prompt Critical rules section. Root cause: AI was returning structurally-valid output for interactive blocks with type-discriminator fields (choices/blanks/pairs) populated but the rich-text fields (prompt_markdown, explanation_markdown, setup_markdown, outcome_markdown) emitted as missing or non-string, causing transformConfigForCanvas to fall through to empty TipTap docs via mdToTipTap(""). Confirmed via lesson_blocks JSONB inspection — first AI Refine on freshly-inserted knowledge_check produced 3 questions with proper choices arrays but every prompt_markdown was `{"type":"doc","content":[{"type":"paragraph"}]}`. **v14→v15 + v12→v13 parity:** Tightened directive to INLINE markdown ONLY (bold, italic, links). Root cause: v14 told AI to populate markdown fields with "real content" — AI interpreted broadly and started emitting `## headings` inside prompt_markdown for ranking and timeline question types. Since mdToTipTap parses only inline marks + paragraphs + hard breaks, heading syntax rendered as literal '##' text in trainee view (visible '## Order the arc of...' and '## What matters most...' before the actual prompts). New v15 directive explicitly enumerates forbidden block-level markdown (no #/##/###, no -/* bullets, no 1./2./3. numbered, no > blockquotes, no ``` code fences, no --- horizontal rules) and explains the failure mode in-prompt. All deploys preserved verify_jwt:false (Class A custom-auth pattern); architecture-reference §61 block parity preserved across both functions. (3) FRONTEND HOT-FIX shipped via Lovable prompt diagnosing AI Refine `lesson_context` bug: BlockEditorPane.tsx handleRefine and IterationModal.tsx full_block branch were BOTH concatenating `JSON.stringify(block.config)` with " --- Change request: " + textarea text into `author_prompt`, sending nothing in `lesson_context`. The AI received its own existing config as the instruction; the user's textarea text was buried after a 5-10KB JSON blob. Diagnosed via super_admin_audit_log query — the author_prompt_excerpt for a failed scenario refine was just the JSON config dump starting with `{"title":null,"intro_markdown":null,"moments":[...]`. Lovable diagnostic prompt run first (no code changes — Lovable reported back the exact concatenation pattern in both files), then fix prompt shipped: send `refineText.trim()` alone as `author_prompt`, send `JSON.stringify(block.config)` as `lesson_context` (the Edge Function's DraftRequest interface already supports it; system prompt formatting wraps it as "Surrounding lesson context for cohesion"). User-confirmed fix worked. Architecture-reference §77 added: AI Refine sends user instruction in `author_prompt` and existing block config in `lesson_context`, never concatenated. (4) Build queue items added (all [POST-LAUNCH]): **Flashcards renderer state reset on AI Refine** — after AI Refine on existing flashcards block, canvas preview shows all cards in reviewed/locked state until Save → reload. Suspected root cause: FlashcardsRender trainee-state object initialized on mount and keyed off per-card client_id; when AI Refine swaps the cards array to a new set, reset effect either doesn't fire or falls through to "completed" default. Fix candidate: mirror pattern in scenario and card_sort renderers — useEffect resetting per-card state when joined client_id list changes. ~5 LOC, single file (BlockRenderer.tsx FlashcardsRender). Not blocking launch (Save fixes it). **Refine textarea voice dictation** — no mic icon for voice input on either BlockEditorPane Refine textarea or IterationModal Refine textarea. (8) Key learnings Session 67: (a) `public.instruments` is canonical source of truth for instrument abbreviation→full name mapping — NOT user memory, NOT any markdown doc; (b) `ai_authoring_context` rows UPDATEd in place despite having a `version` column (table convention is in-place edits, no historical row preservation, no `updated_at` column); (c) right first question on a "function broke" report is "what does the response body actually say" — not "what did I change last"; in this case `{"error":"author_prompt_too_long"}` + audit-log size math made the cause obvious within a few queries; the v11-deploy-as-suspect framing was disproved within one audit-log timestamp query; (d) **MCP `Supabase:get_logs` for `edge-function` is BROKEN in this project** — analytics endpoint returns `INVALID_ARGUMENT: User specified reservation projects/supabase-analytics-ext-queries/locations/EU/reservations/queries-short-12hr is not found`; don't waste a tool call on it, use `pg_net` synthetic HTTP requests + audit-log `after_value->>'edge_function'` filter instead; pg_net pattern: `SELECT net.http_post(url, headers, body) AS request_id;` then separate `SELECT pg_sleep(2); SELECT status_code, content::text FROM net._http_response WHERE id = <id>;` (pg_net is async); (e) `super_admin_audit_log.after_value` (NOT `after_json` as I tried first) — column list verified: id, super_admin_user_id, action_type, company_id, affected_user_id, session_id, detail, created_at, ip_address, user_agent, reason, before_value, after_value, mode, expires_at, ended_at, end_reason; (f) `list_edge_functions` returns are STALE within a single conversation — after a `deploy_edge_function` call, subsequent `list_edge_functions` may still show the old version; use `get_edge_function` against specific slug for fresh state; (g) named-constant extraction trick reinforced — when raising a magic number, extract to a named module-level constant first (`const AUTHOR_PROMPT_MAX_CHARS = 50000`), reference from the validation gate; makes the new value greppable, intent self-documenting, future tuning a one-line change. (9) Standing code-style patterns unchanged from Session 66 (PL/pgSQL structure, Edge Function structure, migration discipline, per-function role boundaries, JSONB schema invariants). No new tables. No migrations. Standing rule §64 added (architecture-reference): backend-frontend ordering for block_type additions — when block parity (§61) cannot complete in one session, prefer backend-ahead-of-frontend over frontend-ahead-of-backend. Backend-ahead means AI may produce blocks that save but don't render (visible bug, easy to spot). Frontend-ahead means the form/renderer exists for a type that the AI can't produce — silent capability gap that's harder to detect. Both are temporary; both close when the matching half ships. Backend-ahead is the safer transient state because rendering failures surface immediately whereas missing AI generation surfaces only when someone tries a workflow that doesn't exist.*

(b) Lead paragraph toolbar toggle visible but clicking had no effect — root cause: TipTap's default TextStyle extension does not declare a fontSize attribute, so setMark("textStyle", { fontSize: "lead" }) calls succeed but the attribute is silently dropped on JSON serialize and never reaches the rendered output; fix requires TextStyle.extend() pattern with custom addAttributes({ fontSize: ... }) that wires parseHTML/renderHTML to a data-font-size HTML attribute; applies to both RichTextEditor (editable mode) AND BlockRenderer (readonly mode); fix bundled into v2 prompt. Post-v2 testing surfaced one final UX issue: slide-in pane stayed anchored to page-top instead of tracking viewport as user scrolled down the stack to edit blocks deep in the lesson. Three iterations to fix (v3 saga): v3 attempted position:sticky inside a flex sibling layout — sticky never engaged because the pane had a CSS transform (for the slide-in animation) which creates a new containing block context that breaks sticky's scroll-context detection in most browsers; v3.1 attempted to separate sticky (outer wrapper) from transform (inner aside) but sticky still didn't engage due to the combination of <main>'s overflow-auto + nested flex containers + the scroll context detection edge case; v3.2 abandoned sticky entirely and switched to position:fixed with explicit pixel offsets (top:56px from AppLayout header height, left:var(--sidebar-width, 0px) referencing the SidebarProvider's CSS variable, bottom:0, width:min(480px, calc(100vw - var(--sidebar-width)))) — open-state worked perfectly but closed-state still visually covered the global AppLayout sidebar because the transform-based slide animation (-translate-x-full) translated the pane from left:256px to visual position [-224px,256px] which overlaps the sidebar's [0,256] range; v3.3 switched from transform-based animation to animating the `left` property directly (closed: left:-480px putting pane fully off-screen in negative coordinate space [-480,0], open: left:var(--sidebar-width)), eliminating any overlap with sidebar's [0,256] range at any animation frame. v3.3 SHIPPED and tested clean: sidebar fully visible at all times (when pane closed, when pane open, during slide animations), pane appears in correct position at viewport top:56px regardless of scroll position, scrolling the stack while pane is open works correctly (pane stays anchored to viewport), all v1+v2 functionality intact. Three new standing rules locked from v3 saga: (a) position:sticky and CSS transform on the same element break sticky engagement — element with transform becomes a new containing block which interferes with sticky's scroll-context detection in most browsers, separate the concerns via nested wrappers if both are needed, or pick fixed positioning instead; (b) position:sticky inside ancestor chains with overflow:auto + nested flex containers is unreliable in this codebase (AppLayout's <main> has overflow-auto creating the scroll context, and nested flex parents introduce edge cases), prefer position:fixed with explicit offsets for any viewport-tracking UI; (c) for slide-in/slide-out pane animations against a global sidebar, animate the `left` property directly rather than using transform, so the closed-state position can be placed in fully negative coordinate space (off-screen) and never visually overlaps the sidebar during transitions. Additional tiptap warning surfaced in console "Duplicate extension names found: ['link']" — logged for future cleanup, non-blocking, likely from the StarterKit including Link by default while RichTextEditor + ReadOnlyTipTap both add Link.configure() explicitly, fix is to drop the explicit Link import and use StarterKit's bundled Link (not addressed Session 60 — added to build queue as cleanup item). Final Session 60 DB state at close: content_item 32e0e966 has 10 active lesson_blocks (text×3, divider, image, heading, embed_audio, quote, list, callout — covers 9 of 9 block types in v1 catalog), 0 lesson_block_drafts rows, image asset 6ce8bc29 active with 1 active version row, audio asset active with 1 active block-scoped ref, 14 successful lesson_blocks_replaced audit rows across the session. ## Session 41 deltas summary

Phase 4 SHIPPED. AIRSA combined report PDF export delivered end-to-end across three Lovable prompts: v1 (initial 5-file build covering generateAirsaPdf.ts, assemblePdfDataForUser.ts assembleAirsaPdfData export, ExportPdfModal AIRSA branch, MyResults dispatcher lift, AirsaCombinedReport onExportClick prop), v2 (four bug fixes: star ★ rendering as ampersand due to WinAnsiEncoding limitation, skill reference one-skill-per-page from incorrect entry-height calculation, top priorities cards splitting from same-shape height bug, methodology footer date showing em-dash placeholder from missing facet_data.generated_at field), v3 (Profile overview heading-orphan + narrow-wrap fix using sectionHeading minContentNeeded argument plus full CONTENT_W - 12 wrap width). Final 9-page PDF rendered cleanly across cover + 14 sections, jsPDF native primitives throughout, text fully selectable, lollipop rendered with native lines/circles preserving STATUS_COLORS canonical mapping including dash pattern on blind_spot only, level-zone shading bands present, ASCII asterisk replaces star glyph in PDF only (on-screen report keeps ★).

Phase 5 strategic frame designed and locked (build deferred to Sessions 42+). Five-tab IA mirroring PTP/NAI canonical structure (Overview / Domains / Skill Inventory / Manager Calibration / Trends + Cross-Instrument). Talent Calibration Index (TCI) locked as headline metric: % of pairs in aligned + confirmed_strength out of all assessed skill-pairs, 0-100 higher is better. Confirmed gaps do NOT count positive (real capability gap, not earned strength). Greatest Growth Opportunities / Strengths to Capitalize paired panels added on Overview tab between sub-metric cards and Calibration Map: top 2 skills + top 2 domains per panel, expand-link for full ranking. Composite Priority Score (CPS) formula locked: cps_growth = (1 - readiness_index) * misalignment_weight where misalignment_weight is bounded [1.0, 2.0] = 1 + (blind_spot_pct + confirmed_gap_pct) / 100; cps_strength = confirmed_strength_pct. Tie-breakers: growth prefers higher blind_spot_pct, strength prefers higher n. Calibration Map confirmed as visual centerpiece: 24-skill × N-departments heatmap using locked STATUS_COLORS by modal status, intensity by status %, priority markers (orange ▲ for top growth, green ◆ for top strength) on row labels tracking the active slice. Manager Calibration tab confirmed for v1 with min-3-reports privacy threshold. Cross-instrument tab confirmed for v1 matching PTP/NAI parity. Schema strategy locked: match PTP/NAI exactly, reuse org_dashboard_narratives with instrument_id = 'INST-003' carrying AIRSA-specific JSONB shape in dimension_scores + narrative_text columns; index_score column carries TCI. Aggregate cadence locked: live RPC computation per dashboard load (mirrors PTP/NAI get_instrument_aggregate pattern), no nightly cron, no aggregate table. AI narrative cached in org_dashboard_narratives, regenerated on user click. Phase 5 split into Phase 5a backend (RPC + Edge Function + schema additions) and Phase 5b frontend (5 tabs of UI) per Phase 3 precedent.

Two architectural learnings logged: (1) jsPDF default helvetica uses WinAnsiEncoding which excludes U+2605 (★); the encoder substitutes a fallback character (observed: ampersand). Loading custom Unicode fonts is heavyweight; safer pattern is to use ASCII-equivalent glyphs in PDFs and reserve Unicode for on-screen contexts. (2) jsPDF splitTextToSize uses the CURRENT font for width calc; setting font BEFORE calling splitTextToSize is the canonical pattern (already commented in generateNaiPdf.ts line 406-407). Skipping this produces correct text but wrong wrap width, causing entries to render at narrow column widths even when full content area is available. Section 6 Profile overview shipped with this bug in v2 and was fixed in v3.

**Two rendering bugs fixed (Prompts 3 + 4).** Both shipped first try.

Prompt 3 — `bodyText` helper in `generateAIRSADashboardPdf.ts`. Two fixes:
1. Font-state leak: `renderContinuationHeader` set 10pt italic and reset weight but not size, causing splitTextToSize-measured 8.5pt lines to render at 10pt and overflow right margin (visible page 3 of first AIRSA PDF). Fix: re-apply `setFontSize(8.5)`, `setFont("helvetica", "normal")`, `setText(BLACK)` inside the for-loop after `checkPageBreak()` and before `doc.text()`.
2. Bullet rendering: split text on `
` first; detect lines matching `/^[-*]\s+(.+)$/` (bullets) or `/^(\d+\.)\s+(.+)$/` (numbered); render with 4mm hanging indent + 1mm extra spacing before each list item; wrapped continuation lines indent past prefix.

Prompt 4 — `renderNarrativeText(text, fontSize, color)` helper inside `AirsaDashboard.tsx`. Splits on `
`, classifies each line, buffers prose into `<p>`, renders bullets as flex rows with `paddingLeft: 16, marginBottom: 4`, numbered items with hanging-indent flex layout. Replaced 7 render points (summary card + 5 expanded narrative subsections + risk flag detail).

**Architectural learnings logged** (added to arch-ref §8):
- jsPDF font-state leak through `renderContinuationHeader` requires re-applying font state on EVERY `doc.text()` call inside a multi-line wrapped-text loop, not just before `splitTextToSize`. The previous §5.6 rule 2 only addressed the measure step, not the render step.
- Frontend bullet rendering for AI-emitted hyphen-prefixed lines requires explicit string-split + line-classification rendering. `whiteSpace: pre-wrap` preserves newlines but provides zero visual hierarchy. Pattern locked in `renderNarrativeText` helper, portable to other dashboards.

**Voice work decision**: AIRSA voice rewrite (this session) was a one-instrument case study. Action-Oriented Voice Redesign across NAI/PTP individual report and dashboard surfaces remains in build queue. Sequencing matters: Voice Redesign should ship BEFORE Org Overview, otherwise the Overview will surface NAI/PTP narratives in the old clinical voice while AIRSA shows the new voice — inconsistent.

Stat fix prompt: `pendingInvitationsCount` filter corrected to exclude revoked + expired rows (was showing 23 instead of 21).

**email_logs table shipped (Option A + Option B).** Schema: id, email_type, recipient_email, subject, resend_message_id, send_status (sent|failed), error_message, source, sent_at, delivered_at, bounced_at, complained_at, last_status_event, last_status_at. RLS: super_admin SELECT only via account_type check, service role bypasses. 4 indexes (recipient_sent_at, resend_message_id partial, failures partial, problem_events partial). pg_cron `purge_email_logs_90d` daily 03:00 UTC. `send-email` v8: `logEmailDispatch` helper writing to email_logs on every code path with optional `email_type` and `source` parameters (default `unknown`). Captures Resend message_id.

**Resend webhook integration shipped.** `resend-webhook` Edge Function v1 verifies Svix signature (HMAC-SHA256 with `whsec_` prefix stripped), 5-minute timestamp freshness window. Looks up email_logs by resend_message_id, updates delivery status. If no match (Auth-system email), inserts new row with `email_type='auth_or_external'`. Endpoint: `https://svprhtzawnbzmumxnhsq.supabase.co/functions/v1/resend-webhook`. Subscribed events: email.sent, email.delivered, email.bounced, email.complained, email.delivery_delayed. Secret stored in Supabase Edge Function Secrets as `RESEND_WEBHOOK_SECRET`. Verified end-to-end: send-email writes row → Resend processes → webhook fires ~1s later → delivered_at populated.

**`coach_invitation_resend` Edge Function v1 shipped.** Per-client scope: clicking Resend on any pending row reminds client about ALL pending instruments under that coach. 24-hour rate limit per recipient_email + email_type='coach_reminder_pending' enforced via email_logs query. Class A JWT auth via auth.getClaims. shareable_link rows treated as first-send template ("Your coach prepared an assessment for you"). Other sources use reminder template ("Reminder: Your BrainWise Assessment is Waiting"). Error codes: unauthorized, not_found, rate_limited, nothing_to_remind, send_failed. PendingInvitations.tsx Resend button wired up with handleResend → toast variants per result. Rate limit verified end-to-end (second click within 24h returns "Reminder already sent recently" toast).

**Expiry sweep + auto-refund automation shipped.** Schema additions to `coach_clients`: `refunded_at`, `stripe_refund_id`, `refund_amount`, `refund_failure_reason`. Index on refunded_at DESC partial. New Edge Function `sweep_expired_invitations` v3 (Class C cron auth via `DISPATCHER_SHARED_SECRET` env, matches dispatch-grace-reminders convention). Filter: expires_at IS NOT NULL AND expires_at < NOW() AND revoked_at IS NULL AND assessment_id IS NULL. Per-row: stamps revoked_at → `recalcCouponAfterRevoke` (deletes Stripe coupon if last row, else recreates at lower amount) → `processAutoRefund` (per refund policy gate). Trigger metadata: `auto_expiry_sweep`. `coach_invitation_revoke` v3: added `processAutoRefund` helper alongside existing `recalcCouponAfterRevoke`. Trigger metadata: `manual_revoke`. Returns `refund: {refunded, amount, refund_id, reason}` in response. pg_cron `sweep_expired_coach_invitations` schedule moved from raw SQL UPDATE to `net.http_post` calling sweep_expired_invitations Edge Function. Schedule `45 3 * * *` (03:45 UTC daily, staggered after email_logs purge at 03:00 and dispatch_grace_reminders at 03:15). Vault secret name: `departure_dispatcher_shared_secret`.

**Locked refund policy (decision):**
- Auto-refund eligibility gate (ALL must be true): `coupon_redeemed = false AND assessment_id IS NULL AND payment_age <= 90 days AND payment_intent_id IS NOT NULL AND coupon_amount > 0`
- Both manual revoke AND automatic expiry trigger auto-refund through same `processAutoRefund` helper
- Individual purchases: 14-day refund window if assessment not started; manual processing only (no auto-refund Edge Function)
- Corporate contracts: all sales final per executed contract
- Verified end-to-end: real $29.99 refund processed against pi_3TVBck2FY7qIyIXA0xp2yuMN, refund_id `re_3TVBck2FY7qIyIXA0oApv0dD`, full pipeline (revoke → coupon deletion → refund → DB stamp) executed in ~1 second

**Schema additions to `assessment_purchases` for individual refund tracking** (manual processing only, no auto-refund): `refunded_at`, `stripe_refund_id`, `refund_amount`, `refund_failure_reason`, `refund_processed_by` (UUID FK users — audits which super_admin approved the refund).

**Terms of Service updated to v2** (effective May 9, 2026). Section 5.3 Coach-paid client assessments rewritten to reference auto-refund policy. Section 5.5 Refund policy rewritten with three buckets (Individual / Coach-paid / Corporate) and explicit eligibility rules. ## Session 49 deltas summary

Group A audit prequel SHIPPED + Group A Feature A1 Tier 1 backend SHIPPED. Larger than scoped at session open (originally just the prequel), but kept entirely backend-only and verified end-to-end before close. Cohort timeline preserved (Plan A confirmed: A1 frontend in Session 50, Group C starts Session 51).

**Audit log schema additions.** `super_admin_audit_log` got 9 new columns (ip_address, user_agent, reason, before_value, after_value, mode, expires_at, ended_at, end_reason) plus 2 new partial indexes (mode, session_id). `company_admin_audit_log` got 4 new columns (reason, before_value, after_value, super_admin_acting_as_user_id with FK to users) plus 1 partial index. Both tables had RLS preserved unchanged.

**Option C lookup table.** Replaced `super_admin_audit_log_action_type_check` CHECK constraint (15 hardcoded strings) with FK to new `public.super_admin_action_types` table. 19 action types seeded across 8 categories (15 carried from CHECK + 4 new for impersonation: impersonation_started, impersonation_ended, impersonation_action, impersonation_denied_action). Table includes metadata columns (requires_mfa, requires_justification, is_mutation, denylist_during_impersonation) for future enforcement use.

**`log_super_admin_action()` helper RPC.** Standardized argument signature `(p_target_user_id, p_target_org_id, p_action_type, p_before, p_after, p_reason, p_mode)`, returns inserted row's UUID. Actor derivation reads `request.jwt.claims` for `imp_actor_user_id` (Path 3 — works correctly pre-A1 with auth.uid() fallback AND post-A1 with impersonation claims). Session id from `imp_session_id` claim if present (so audit_session_replay groups all events from one impersonation). Mode prefixed with `impersonation:<imp_mode>:` when in impersonation context. Caller responsibility to gate on assert_super_admin (helper does NOT self-gate because in dual-attribution land auth.uid() = impersonated user).

**A1 impersonation infrastructure.** New `impersonation_sessions` table with immutability trigger (only ended_at + end_reason mutable, never DELETE), unique-active-per-admin INDEX (DB-level nested impersonation prevention), no-self-impersonation CHECK, justification length >= 10 CHECK. `validate_impersonation_session()` SECURITY DEFINER STABLE for cheap repeated calls. `assert_impersonation_allows()` enforces 9-category denylist mapped to scope 2.3.1-2.3.9 (identity_change, assessment_submission, privacy_consent, financial_transaction, outbound_user_communication, permission_change, corporate_admin_action, coach_action, lifecycle_action). Mode read from DB row not JWT (defense in depth).

**Custom Access Token Hook for impersonation claims.** `public.custom_access_token_hook(event jsonb)` injects imp_session_id, imp_actor_user_id, imp_mode, imp_expires_at into JWTs at issuance time. Auth method gate: only fires on `magiclink` or `token_refresh` (prevents target user's normal logins from inheriting impersonation context). EXCEPTION WHEN OTHERS wrapper ensures hook errors NEVER break platform auth. Cole registered hook in Dashboard → Auth → Hooks. 4 unit tests passing (no-session passthrough, auth-method-gate-blocks-password, magiclink-injects-all-four-claims, malformed-event-safe-fallback).

**MFA freshness via `check_mfa_freshness()`.** Service-role-only RPC reading `auth.mfa_amr_claims` for the caller's session, returns boolean for "TOTP within last p_max_age_seconds." Used by impersonation-start to enforce fresh-MFA gate (scope 2.2.7). Pattern B confirmed (Supabase Auth supports mid-session TOTP via auth.mfa.challenge() + auth.mfa.verify()).

**Three new Edge Functions.** `impersonation-start` v1: 8-gate pipeline (auth → super_admin → fresh MFA → target exists → not self → no nested → mode valid → justification valid), insert sessions row, write audit, generateLink + verifyOtp produces target-user session, hook decorates JWT with imp_* claims. Rollback on any post-insert failure. `impersonation-end` v1: ends session via impersonation token, dual-attribution audit row writes correctly via JWT-claim-aware helper. `sweep_expired_impersonation_sessions` v1: Class C cron auth, ends expired-but-not-ended sessions with end_reason='timeout', uses direct INSERT into super_admin_audit_log (cron-context exception since log_super_admin_action requires auth.uid()). Verified end-to-end: pre-expired test session swept, audit row written, ended_at = expires_at exactly.

**`*/5 * * * *` cron schedule.** `sweep_expired_impersonation_sessions` runs every 5 minutes (not the daily/15-min stagger convention) because impersonation sessions are 30-minute lifecycle. Worst-case post-expiry session lingering = 5 minutes server-side; frontend client-side timeout enforces the user-visible countdown.

**`_shared/impersonation_gate.ts` helper module.** Canonical Tier 2 enforcement helper. Exports `enforceImpersonationGate(client, category)` returning `{gated: false}` or `{gated: true, ...}` or throwing `ImpersonationDeniedError`. Plus `logImpersonationAction()` for callers to write impersonation_action audit rows after allowed mutations. Module deployed via `test-impersonation-gate` Edge Function (test-only) to validate bundling. Probe with no-auth confirmed clean 401 — module bundling resolved correctly.

**Edge Function reconnaissance complete.** Surveyed all 52 deployed Edge Functions (48 pre-Session 49 + 4 added this session). 27 require Tier 2 gating per scope 2.6.3 expanded for new functions (AIRSA supervisor flow, Group D coach functions, lifecycle functions, set-account-type — none of which were in the original scope's ~12-function list). 25 explicitly do not need gating with documented rationale: 8 per-user AI functions (user-scoped, ownership-checked), 3 cron, 2 webhook, 2 read-only, 3 internal helpers, 3 impersonation infrastructure, 3 public unauthenticated forms, 1 admin utility. Recon doc captured in Session 49→50 handoff.

**Architectural decision: Custom Access Token Hook over separate cookie.** Analyzed three options (JWT manual mint, separate cookie, Custom Access Token Hook). Chose Custom Access Token Hook with auth_method gate. Rationale: lowest build cost (~1 session backend vs 2-3 for cookie), preserves existing helper RPCs (no rework), single signed channel for SOC 2 defensibility, hook errors cannot break platform auth (EXCEPTION wrapper). Decision documented inline in custom_access_token_hook function comments.

**Edge Function `verify_jwt: false` convention preserved.** All Session 49 Edge Functions use `verify_jwt: false` with explicit `auth.getClaims` inside the function body. Matches existing convention. Build queue item: consider migration toward `verify_jwt: true` as SOC 2 hardening pass.

One architectural delta surfaced and logged in architecture-reference.md §23.7: `Supabase:deploy_edge_function` prepends `source/` to the entrypoint_path automatically. Pass `entrypoint_path: "index.ts"` (naked, no prefix). Passing `source/index.ts` causes path doubling and BadRequestException. Discovered during the `generate-dashboard-narrative` deploy: first attempt with `source/index.ts` failed, retry with naked `index.ts` succeeded. This corrects/clarifies §23.2 which had implied the entrypoint_path was passed verbatim.

Read App.tsx, AppLayout.tsx, RoleGuard.tsx, ProtectedRoute.tsx, MfaChallenge.tsx, MfaEnrollment.tsx, useAuth.tsx, useUserProfile.tsx, useSuperAdminSession.tsx, AppSidebar.tsx, Settings.tsx, CompanyAccounts.tsx, PlatformHealth.tsx. Six integration decisions locked, captured in architecture-reference.md §25:

1. Banner injection at App.tsx-level (NOT AppLayout) so banner persists on bypass-AppLayout protected routes (Onboarding, MFA enrollment, demographic-form).

3. Impersonate entry: NEW `/super-admin/users` page (universal user search + row actions), NOT PlatformHealth or CompanyAccounts. Universal across account types, future actions slot in cleanly.

5. `ProtectedRoute` does NOT bypass demographic/MFA/deactivation gates during impersonation (Option B locked) — Tier 2 backend denylist is the security layer.

Three-prompt sequencing locked for Session 53:

- **Phase C-1**: ImpersonationProvider + ImpersonationBanner + ImpersonationChrome + MfaChallenge `onCancel` additive + App.tsx wiring + Tier 2 denylist audit.
- **Phase C-2**: SuperAdminUsers page + JustificationModal + sidebar nav update + redirectByRole update + impersonation-start/impersonation-end integration.
- **Phase D**: AccessHistory page + sidebar settings update + route registration.

Architecture-reference.md §20 schema clarification logged in §24.6: §20.1 and §20.2 ALTER TABLEs are CORRECT and verified against live DB. The actor column on `super_admin_audit_log` is `super_admin_user_id`, target is `affected_user_id`, org is `company_id`, jsonb detail is `detail`. The actor column on `company_admin_audit_log` is `actor_user_id`, target is `target_user_id`, org is `organization_id`, jsonb detail is `action_details`. Names matter for any RPC writing or filtering against these tables.

## Session 53 deltas summary

Phase C-1 pre-flight backend SHIPPED. Three Edge Function/migration deliveries unblocked the Phase C-1 Lovable prompt and closed two security gaps that Session 52 architectural decisions had assumed already covered.

**impersonation-end v2 (Session 53)**: Modified to mint fresh super admin tokens via generateLink + verifyOtp pattern (mirrors impersonation-start). Returns `{ success, restored: true, super_admin_user_id, access_token, refresh_token, expires_at }` at top level. Critical sequencing: ended_at set BEFORE generateLink fires, guaranteeing custom_access_token_hook does not stamp imp_* claims on the restored super admin token. Failure path returns `{ restored: false, restore_error }` with HTTP 200 — session is still ended at DB level even if token mint fails; frontend signs out and redirects to /login. Architecture-reference §26.1.

**is_impersonating() and is_impersonating_act() helpers + user_demographics RLS WITH CHECK (Session 53)**: Two SECURITY DEFINER STABLE helpers that read JWT claims for active impersonation, defense-in-depth verifying against impersonation_sessions DB row. Both granted EXECUTE to authenticated. user_demographics policy refactored from FOR ALL into split policies: SELECT allowed regardless of impersonation context (super admin observers can read), but INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE require NOT is_impersonating(). Both observe AND act mode block writes. Verification matrix passed all five scenarios. Architecture-reference §26.2.

**identity-mutation Edge Function v1 (Session 53)**: Single chokepoint for identity_change category mutations going through Supabase auth APIs (auth.updateUser for password/email; auth.mfa.enroll/unenroll). Class A explicit (verify_jwt=false; auth.getClaims inside). Calls enforceImpersonationGate("identity_change") first, raises 403 IMPERSONATION_DENIED for any impersonation context. Forwards via callerClient (pattern Z) so auth.mfa.enroll/unenroll work natively. Phase C-1.5 frontend rewires (folded into Phase C-1 prompt) point ResetPassword.tsx, Settings.tsx saveEmail, MfaEnrollment.tsx handleEnroll, and any unenroll surface at the wrapper. Architecture-reference §26.3.

**§25.9 partial reversal locked**: Original Session 52 decision that ProtectedRoute does NOT bypass demographic/MFA/deactivation gates during impersonation rested on the assumption that the Tier 2 backend denylist alone covered all paths. That assumption was false (RLS-only direct writes and Supabase auth APIs bypass the gate). With §26.2 and §26.3 closing the database and application paths, the frontend complement is to ALSO redirect /onboarding, /demographic-consent, /demographic-form, /mfa-enrollment, /peer-sharing-optin to /dashboard during impersonation. Defense in depth, three layers. Architecture-reference §26.4.

**Phase C-2 hotfix (mid-session 53)**: `/super-admin/users` page crashed with blank screen + console TypeError when search results contained any user with `account_type IS NULL`. Two production users in this state (`test@test.com`, `testclientbwe+testnewuser@gmail.com`) — both half-finished signups where the user authenticated but never picked an account type. Root cause: `formatAccountType` and `accountTypeBadgeVariant` in Users.tsx called `.split(...)` and `switch` on null. Fixed at the backend layer by patching `search_impersonation_targets` to `COALESCE(account_type, 'unknown')` so the RPC contract effectively guarantees a string. Frontend null-guards (Layer 2) added as defense in depth via small follow-up Lovable prompt. Schema-level fix to `users.account_type` nullability deferred — see new build queue item below.

**Three new build queue items logged (Session 53 mid)**:

- **MEDIUM (post-launch)**: Refactor `current_user_mfa_satisfied()` from factor-existence check to session-AAL check. Currently a user with a verified factor returns mfaSatisfied=true regardless of session aal1/aal2 — weaker than Supabase native AAL-based enforcement. Required for proper post-impersonation re-MFA flow. Architecture-reference §26.6.
- **LOW (post-launch)**: Replace hardcoded `v_denylist text[]` array in `assert_impersonation_allows` with a SELECT against a new `super_admin_denylist_categories` table. Drop the vestigial `super_admin_action_types.denylist_during_impersonation` column in the same migration. Benefits: queryable denylist for SOC 2 evidence collection. Architecture-reference §26.5.
- **LOW (post-launch)**: Audit other RLS-only direct-write tables for impersonation gaps. user_demographics was the obvious one; sweep for `users` self-update fields, `user_subscription_preferences`, `user_results_consent` etc. Add `NOT is_impersonating()` to WITH CHECK on any table where a super admin should not be able to mutate as the target.
- **MEDIUM (post-launch)**: Investigate and clean up `users.account_type IS NULL` rows. Currently 2 users in this state (1 marked is_internal_test=true, 1 marked false despite testclientbwe email pattern). Either backfill to `individual` based on signup intent, or constrain the column NOT NULL once data is clean. Today's hotfix masks the symptom at the RPC layer (COALESCE to 'unknown') but the underlying schema permits a state that no UX can produce intentionally.
- **HOOK HARDENING SHIPPED Session 53 close**: `custom_access_token_hook` now distinguishes legitimate impersonation-start token mints from stranded-session contamination. For `'otp'`/`'magiclink'` initial mints, the hook requires the matching `impersonation_sessions` row was created < 60 seconds ago (impersonation-start mints within ~2s; stranded rows are minutes+ old). For `'token_refresh'`, the hook requires the incoming JWT already carries `imp_session_id` matching the active row (refreshes preserve, never create). Investigated `auth.sessions` DELETE trigger as alternative; Supabase does NOT delete auth.sessions on logout (only expires them via expires_at), so a delete trigger would never fire on signOut events. The hook freshness gate solves the same problem at the right layer. Stranded rows still get cleaned by the existing 30-min cron sweep, but they can no longer pollute subsequent target-user logins while pending cleanup.

- **NICE-TO-HAVE (post-launch)**: Frontend `SIGNED_OUT` listener that calls `impersonation-end` before the JWT is destroyed. Belt-and-suspenders on top of the hook freshness gate. The user clicks Log Out → ImpersonationProvider's auth state listener catches `SIGNED_OUT` → calls impersonation-end if currently impersonating → updates DB row ended_at promptly. Race condition risk: JWT may already be invalidating by the time the call fires, so impersonation-end could 401. Acceptable — the cron sweep is the floor, the hook gate is the security boundary, this would just clean up the audit timeline faster.
- **LOW (post-launch)**: AccessHistory.tsx frontend null-guard for `formatActionType(action_category)`. Backend defense added in Session 53 (RPC now COALESCEs `action_category` to `'organization_admin_action'` for company_admin source rows), but frontend also calls `.replace()` on the value so a future RPC regression would crash again. Mirror the pattern from Users.tsx null-guard work.

Phase C-1, C-2, D Lovable prompts unblocked. Session 53 continues with frontend prompts.

**Phase C-2 frontend SHIPPED**: One Lovable prompt covering 7 files. 2 new (Users.tsx super admin search page with debounced query, kebab-dropdown action menu per row, separator above destructive Force pseudonymization stub; JustificationModal with two-step flow — justification + mode radio, then embedded MfaChallenge with onCancel back-to-step-1, plus error-code-aware toasts for MFA_REQUIRED/NESTED_IMPERSONATION/SELF_IMPERSONATION/TARGET_NOT_FOUND); 5 modified (ImpersonationProvider extends interface with targetEmail field populated via localStorage stash keyed by session_id, with cleanup in all three endImpersonation branches; ImpersonationBanner displays email when present and falls back to monospace user_id; App.tsx registers /super-admin/users route with RoleGuard + SuperAdminSessionProvider wrapping pattern and replaces /super-admin layout-only fallback with Navigate redirect; useAuth.redirectByRole changes super admin landing from /super-admin/health to /super-admin/users; AppSidebar adds User Management nav entry with UserSearch icon between My Results and Platform Health). Verified file-by-file post-Lovable: kebab-dropdown action pattern with five menu items in correct order, account type badges per the brand mapping (destructive for super_admin, default for org/company admin, secondary for coach, outline for individual/corporate), self-impersonation prevention at UX layer, debounced search at 250ms with p_limit 25, all four table states handled (empty/loading/error/no-results/results). Architecturally Phase C is complete; end-to-end impersonation flow live pending Cole's manual integration test.

**Phase D frontend SHIPPED**: One Lovable prompt covering 3 files. 1 new (AccessHistory.tsx at /settings/access-history — six columns When/Action/Actor/Source/Mode/Reason, source badges destructive=Super Admin/default=Org Admin, mode badges secondary=Observe/outline=Act, pagination 50 per page hidden when single page, Path A CSV export with 200-per-call RPC pagination up to 1000 cap, all states handled). 2 modified (App.tsx registers route as sibling of /settings/billing, no RoleGuard needed since auth wrapper handles it; AppSidebar adds Access History entry to BOTH settingsSubItems and coachSettingsSubItems arrays between Privacy & Permissions and Billing & Receipts using already-imported History icon). Verified file-by-file post-Lovable: pagination logic correct, CSV column structure matches spec, data flowed through cleanly.

**Mid-session hotfixes shipped (Session 53)**:

- search_impersonation_targets COALESCE account_type and paginated default-load (multi-field search across email + full_name + organization_name; total_count window function for pagination; includes self after frontend self-impersonation prevention proven sufficient at UX layer)
- check_mfa_freshness reads BOTH auth.mfa_amr_claims AND auth.mfa_challenges.verified_at (Supabase doesn't write amr_claims rows on subsequent mfa.verify calls of an already-aal2 session; the verified_at fallback bridges this) — Architecture-reference §26.8
- custom_access_token_hook accepts 'otp' as valid impersonation auth method (Supabase records verifyOtp({type:'magiclink'}) as 'otp' regardless of link type), then tightened with 60s freshness gate so stranded sessions can't contaminate normal user logins — Architecture-reference §26.7
- log_super_admin_action skips impersonation: prefix on lifecycle events (impersonation_started, impersonation_ended, impersonation_denied_action) for grouping parity — Architecture-reference §26.9

- identity-mutation friendly error toasts via new src/lib/identityMutation.ts helper that parses error.context.json() for FunctionsHttpError and surfaces "This action is blocked while impersonating" message for IMPERSONATION_DENIED code — Architecture-reference §26.12
